TITLE: Upgrading 3ds Max .NET projects from .NET Framework to .NET 8

<script language="JavaScript">&amp;amp;amp;lt;!--
function msoCommentShow(anchor_id, com_id)
{
	if(msoBrowserCheck()) 
		{
		c = document.all(com_id);
		a = document.all(anchor_id);
		if (null != c &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; null == c.length &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; null != a &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; null == a.length)
			{
			var cw = c.offsetWidth;
			var ch = c.offsetHeight;
			var aw = a.offsetWidth;
			var ah = a.offsetHeight;
			var x  = a.offsetLeft;
			var y  = a.offsetTop;
			var el = a;
			while (el.tagName != &amp;amp;amp;quot;BODY&amp;amp;amp;quot;) 
				{
				el = el.offsetParent;
				x = x + el.offsetLeft;
				y = y + el.offsetTop;
				}
			var bw = document.body.clientWidth;
			var bh = document.body.clientHeight;
			var bsl = document.body.scrollLeft;
			var bst = document.body.scrollTop;
			if (x + cw + ah / 2 &amp;amp;amp;gt; bw + bsl &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; x + aw - ah / 2 - cw &amp;amp;amp;gt;= bsl ) 
				{ c.style.left = x + aw - ah / 2 - cw; }
			else 
				{ c.style.left = x + ah / 2; }
			if (y + ch + ah / 2 &amp;amp;amp;gt; bh + bst &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; y + ah / 2 - ch &amp;amp;amp;gt;= bst ) 
				{ c.style.top = y + ah / 2 - ch; }
			else 
				{ c.style.top = y + ah / 2; }
			c.style.visibility = &amp;amp;amp;quot;visible&amp;amp;amp;quot;;
}	}	}
function msoCommentHide(com_id) 
{
	if(msoBrowserCheck())
		{
		c = document.all(com_id);
		if (null != c &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; null == c.length)
		{
		c.style.visibility = &amp;amp;amp;quot;hidden&amp;amp;amp;quot;;
		c.style.left = -1000;
		c.style.top = -1000;
		} } 
}
function msoBrowserCheck()
{
	ms = navigator.appVersion.indexOf(&amp;amp;amp;quot;MSIE&amp;amp;amp;quot;);
	vers = navigator.appVersion.substring(ms + 5, ms + 6);
	ie4 = (ms &amp;amp;amp;gt; 0) &amp;amp;amp;amp;&amp;amp;amp;amp; (parseInt(vers) &amp;amp;amp;gt;= 4);
	return ie4;
}

{

</p>
<div class="WordSection1">
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">3ds Max 2025 and earlier versions have used the .NET Framework for building plugins, but, with the VFX world transitioning to .NET, 3ds Max 2026 brings this support with it. As such, .NET projects require a bit of housekeeping to get them compiled and working in .NET 8 for our case. This blog is a simple walkthrough of the upgrade process, using the public `Explode Geometry` Sample hosted on our ADN GitHub Page <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>.</p>
<h2 class="MsoNormal"><strong><span class="Heading2Char"><span style="font-size: 16.0pt; line-height: 116%;">The Upgrade Assistant</span></span></strong></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">Microsoft provides an <a href="https://dotnet.microsoft.com/en-us/platform/upgrade-assistant" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Upgrade Assistant</a> extension to help with porting .NET Framework projects to .NET as well as .NET Core to .NET and much more. The tool simplifies and aids in handling the upgrade intricacies, leaving just a few more steps for us to complete.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">First, to get things going, check if you have the Upgrade Assistant installed. If not installed, the Visual Studio Extensions Manager should be your first stop. With Visual Studio opened, navigate to <em>Menu &gt; Extensions &gt; Manage Extensions. Under the Extensions Manager</em>, search for &#39;Upgrade Assistant&#39; and get it installed as shown below.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6305200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image002" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6305200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6305200b-800wi" title="Image002" /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">With the assistant downloaded, follow the instructions to get it installed. This may include having to restart the IDE to get the extension installed and loaded for use.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">Please note that the Upgrade Assistant is available as both a Visual Studio extension and a command-line utility. In this blog, we will only cover using the Visual Studio extension.</p>
<h2 style="margin: 14.95pt 0cm 14.95pt 0cm;"><strong><span style="font-size: 18.0pt; line-height: 116%; font-family: &#39;Aptos&#39;,sans-serif;">Explode Geometry Project .NET Upgrade</span></strong></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">Let&#39;s work with our <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry" rel="noopener" target="_blank">ADN Explode Geometry</a><span style="font-family: Consolas;"> Sample</span>&#0160;available on GitHub and see how we can get it building and running in .NET 8.</p>
<h3 style="margin: 14.05pt 0cm 14.05pt 0cm;"><strong>Fetching the project</strong></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">This is an easy step: clone the repo (SSH, HTTPS, ZIP, or any format you prefer). For this step, we will clone the branch on tag v2.7 as the repo is already updated to support .NET.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;"><a></a><code><a><span style="font-family: Consolas;">git clone --branch v2.7 https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry<br /></span></a><span style="font-family: Consolas;">cd <a>3dsMax-Explode-Geometry</a></span></code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">In the Source folder, open the <span style="font-family: Consolas;">.csproj</span> in Visual Studio.</p>
<h3 style="margin: 14.05pt 0cm 14.05pt 0cm;"><strong>Upgrading to .NET, the Assistant-way</strong></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">As detailed in the <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/dotnet/core/porting/upgrade-assistant-overview">Microsoft Blog</a> on the assistant, we can upgrade by Right Clicking the project &gt; Upgrade &gt; A new project upgrade page is opened.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">Here, we select the project upgrade way and work with `<span style="font-family: Consolas;">in place project upgrade`</span> but feel free to test the other options if it suits your needs.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861024f9a200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image003" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e861024f9a200d image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861024f9a200d-800wi" title="Image003" /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">With the upgrade type ironed out, next we need to select the .NET version to upgrade to. For our case, we are going for .NET 8.0 LTS; this is the expectation for 3ds Max 2026 .NET plugins. You may get an action requirement to download and install .NET SDK if you don&#39;t have it yet; if so, proceed with that installation, then pick it up from here once done.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6359200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image004" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6359200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6359200b-800wi" title="Image004" /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">In the next step, we are required to select the files to upgrade. By default, all files in the project are checked, including the project file. Let&#39;s leave it as is and proceed with upgrading the selection. After the process completes, if no errors came up, then our project will have been transformed. Probably, the project will try to build but fail; we will fix that shortly. To check the logs, switch the combo box as shown below to the <span style="font-family: Consolas;">Upgrade Assistant</span> option.<a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861024fae200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><br /><br /></a><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861025005200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image005" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e861025005200d image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861025005200d-800wi" title="Image005" /></a><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861024fae200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><br /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">At the end of this process, you should have a project file `.csproj` that has been updated to conform to the .NET 8 project format. Running a build fails due to missing references to the Autodesk assemblies that may have been dropped in the upgrade.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">To fix the missing Autodesk assemblies or any other internal or 3rd-party assemblies, we can achieve that either by</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal">Directly edit the <strong><em>csproj</em></strong> file by copying the <strong><em><span style="font-family: Consolas;">ItemGroup</span></em></strong> for the assemblies from the old project file and updating where necessary. For instance, for the <span style="font-family: Consolas;">Autodesk.Max.dll</span> assembly, we can have it included in the new project file as shown below, with the version updated to 2026 - of course. The same will be done for the other project dependencies like <span style="font-family: Consolas;">CSharpUtilities.dll</span>, <span style="font-family: Consolas;">ManagedServices.dll</span>, etc.<br /><br /><code>&lt;ItemGroup&gt; </code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;Reference Include=&quot;Autodesk.Max&quot;&gt; </code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;HintPath&gt;$(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2026)\Autodesk.Max.dll&lt;/HintPath&gt; </code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;/Reference&gt; <br />&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;.... other assemblies </code><br /><code>&lt;/ItemGroup&gt;</code></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst">A<a></a><a>nother way is making use of the Visual Studio </a><span style="font-family: Consolas;">Reference Manager</span> that is accessed from the <code>Menu &gt; Project &gt; Add Project Reference &gt; Browse</code> &amp; find your assemblies. Once all intended libraries are selected, click OK to add them. Just as in the option above, the new assemblies will be added back into the project file. Just FYI, we can change the assembly paths for the Autodesk assemblies to make use of the path variables. This way, any user can use our plugin despite the installation path they chose. For our case, we will use the path as <span style="font-family: Consolas;">$(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2026)\&lt;assembly name&gt;</span>.</li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle" style="margin-bottom: 0cm;">&#0160;</p>
<p class="MsoListParagraphCxSpLast" style="margin-bottom: 0cm;"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6321200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image006" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6321200b img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860eb6321200b-800wi" title="Image006" /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">At this stage, we can build our project, and everything should now be okay. But, looking at the logs, our build outputs are going to the default Visual Studio project build directory and not the one defined under our debug/release property group. <a>In .NET Framework project configuration, we had defined <code>&lt;OutputPath&gt;</code> inside each build type (Build/Debug). In .NET, we define it inside the <code>&lt;PropertyGroup&gt;</code>, where we have our project defaults as shown below:</a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;"><code><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Consolas;">&lt;PropertyGroup&gt; <br /></span><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Consolas;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;TargetFramework&gt;net8.0-windows&lt;/TargetFramework&gt; <br /></span><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Consolas;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;... the other config here &lt;OutputPath&gt;C:\Our\intended\path\for\the\assembly&lt;/OutputPath&gt;<br /></span><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; font-family: Consolas;">&lt;/PropertyGroup&gt;</span></code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">For our case, we will be using the Autodesk plugin path as our output path. This way, any plugin development changes can be updated in the sample.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">Note: There may be extra steps to getting the assembly loaded into 3ds Max. If using <span style="font-family: Consolas;">PackageContents.xml</span>, update where necessary to get the assembly and its dependencies loaded. Refer to the following documentation pages for help: <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2026/ENU/?guid=menu_migration_guide" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Menu System Porting</a>, <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=packaging_plugins" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span class="MsoHyperlink">Packaging Samples</span></a></p>
<h2 style="margin: 14.95pt 0cm 14.95pt 0cm;"><strong><span style="font-size: 18.0pt; line-height: 116%; font-family: &#39;Aptos&#39;,sans-serif;">Final Housekeeping</span></strong></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 12.0pt 0cm 12.0pt 0cm;">As a close, we need to do a bit of housekeeping. Here are a few things to consider:</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal">Setting included assemblies as not private: When we add assembly references in our project, the build process ends up copying the assembly references and their dependencies to the `OutputPath` directory, which is not the intended behavior. This results in duplication of assemblies, which may cause 3ds Max to crash. To resolve this, update each of the included assemblies as follows:<br /><br /><code><em><span lang="EN-US" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&lt;Reference Include=&quot;ManagedServices&quot;&gt;<br /></span></em><em style="text-indent: 36pt;"><span lang="FR" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;HintPath&gt;<br /></span></em><em><span lang="FR" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;$(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2026)\ManagedServices.dll <br /></span></em><em><span lang="FR" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;/HintPath&gt;<br /></span></em><em style="text-indent: 36pt;"><span lang="FR" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;Private&gt; false &lt;/Private&gt;<br /></span></em></code><em><span lang="FR" style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;"><code>&lt;/Reference&gt;</code><br /><br /></span></em></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle">Disabling the <code>AppendTargetFrameworkToOutputPath</code> flag: Since plugins for 3ds Max are meant for Windows, we can disable the flag above to ensure the assemblies don&#39;t end up nested in a target framework directory.<br /><br /><code><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&lt;AppendTargetFrameworkToOutputPath &gt;false&lt;/ AppendTargetFrameworkToOutputPath &gt;</span></em></code></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal"><em><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; line-height: 116%;">&#0160;</span></em>Updating/bumping up plugin versions. This applies to both <span style="font-family: Consolas;">ApplicationVersion</span> and <span style="font-family: Consolas;">AssemblyVersion</span> keys.</li>
<li class="MsoNormal">Adding additional library information that was maybe dropped in the upgrade or new in the new project version. For instance, <span style="font-family: Consolas;">FileVersion</span><span style="text-indent: -18pt;">, </span><span style="font-family: Consolas;">AssemblyVersion</span><span style="text-indent: -18pt;">, etc.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoListParagraphCxSpLast" style="margin-bottom: 0cm; text-indent: -18.0pt;"><span style="font-family: Symbol;"> <span style="font: 7.0pt &#39;Times New Roman&#39;;">&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160; </span></span>You can find the full sample and code in our <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry" rel="noopener" target="_blank">ADN Github Repo</a>.</p>
</div>

TITLE: What's new in 3ds Max 2026?
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: whats-new-in-3ds-max-2026
CATEGORY: .NET API

-----
BODY:
<div class="WordSection1">
<p class="MsoNormal"><br />A few weeks ago, 3ds Max 2026 saw its official release, introducing new features and capabilities for both artists and developers. With this release, 3ds Max saw many upgrades in <em>Arnold to 5.8</em>, <em>Substance to 3.0.8</em>, <em>performance improvements</em> in different modifiers, and much more. Refer to the <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2026/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2026_sdk" rel="noopener" target="_blank">release page</a> for a detailed feature change for 3ds Max 2026.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861022524200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image001" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e861022524200d img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e861022524200d-800wi" title="Image001" /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><em>Image courtesy of Mohanad Hossam</em></p>
<h2>SDK Changes</h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">First, let&#39;s discuss the SDK changes that came with 3ds Max 2025 last year. We didn&#39;t have full information then, as there were breaking changes that are now fully documented.</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal"><span style="font: 7.0pt &#39;Times New Roman&#39;;">&#0160;</span>3ds Max 2025 came with a revamped new menu system. The update necessitates the rewriting of all plugins that generate menus or quad menus to align with 3ds Max 2025. Check out more information on the <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=GUID-FF48D0EC-6669-4EC7-AB43-E9998A14A198" rel="noopener" target="_blank">menu changes</a>, <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2026/ENU/?guid=menu_migration_guide" rel="noopener" target="_blank">menu migration guide</a>, and <a href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2025/05/porting-plugins-from-3ds-max-2024-to-3ds-max-2025.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">general plugin migration guide to 2025 using the Explode Geometry Sample</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoNormal">With that out of the way, what&#39;s new in 2026?</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal">NET 8.0 Support: In 2026, .NET 8 support for plugin development was introduced to align with Autodesk&#39;s goal of updating all our projects to more modern standards. This upgrade is a shift from the framework-based projects of previous 3ds Max versions; as such, this breaking change will require project restructuring and rebuilding to work in 2026. Refer to our <a href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2025/05/upgrading-3ds-max-net-projects-from-net-framework-to-net-8.html%20" rel="noopener" target="_blank">porting guide from .NET Framework to .NET for plugins</a>.</li>
<li class="MsoNormal">Lots of minor API changes in ActionTable, Animatable, CustCont, ColorManagement, Menu System, etc. for performance and/or added functionality.</li>
<li class="MsoNormal">SDK licensing updates: SDK header licenses have been updated for conformity to the Autodesk license agreement, which is provided at the time of installation or download.</li>
<li class="MsoNormal">Updated samples and documentation to reflect API changes.</li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoNormal">Refer to our <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2026/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2026_sdk" rel="noopener" target="_blank"> What s New </a>docs section for a full list of API &amp; SDK changes in 2026.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">&#0160;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">&#0160;</p>
</div>

KEYWORDS:

--------
AUTHOR: Allan K. Koech
AUTHOR EMAIL: allan.koech@autodesk.com
TITLE: Porting Plugins from 3ds Max 2024 to 3ds Max 2025
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: porting-plugins-from-3ds-max-2024-to-3ds-max-2025
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: CuiActionCommandAdapter
CATEGORY: MAXScript

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2025/05/porting-plugins-from-3ds-max-2024-to-3ds-max-2025.html 
DATE: 05/28/2025 08:54:10 AM
-----
BODY:
<div class="WordSection1">
<p class="MsoNormal"><img height="387" src="https://www.borndigital.co.jp/app/uploads/2024/04/10_news_3dsmax2025_page-1040x450.jpg" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" width="894" /></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">3ds Max 2025 came with some breaking changes that marked an era of new approaches aimed at improving performance at the core. As a result, some tools tailored to pre-2025 3ds Max versions may fail to load into 2025. In this blog, we will give you a walkthrough of how to handle porting a plugin to 2025, using one of our samples as an example.</p>
<h2>What Changed in 2025?</h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">2025 brings some exciting changes; here are some highlights:</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><em><strong>Menu Changes</strong></em>: 3ds Max 2025 introduces an overhaul of the menu system, deprecating the old MenuManager <em>(menuMan)</em> and introducing the new CuiMenuManager and its associated classes. This brings more ways of creating menus, statically or dynamically.</li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>shape.h</em></strong>: Introduced 8 helper methods for enhanced Bezier shape handling and end cap material options to improve shape rendering and control.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>spline3d.h</em></strong>: Added methods for checking spline segment linearity , managing angle constraints, and enhancing spline manipulation capabilities.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>splshape.h</em></strong>: Implemented methods to override spline closure prompts, providing customizable control over user interface prompts.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>mnmesh.h</em></strong>: Introduced new classes and optimizations for vertex origins and mesh management, focusing on performance improvements with complex meshes.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><strong><em>Mesh.h</em></strong>: We have added a helper method in <em>ScopedLockChannels</em> to efficiently update transformed bounding boxes, thereby enhancing mesh rendering accuracy.</li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>MaxGuid.h</em></strong>: Introduced the MaxGuid class for GUID management within MaxSDK, facilitating efficient unique identifier handling.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>iparamm2.h</em></strong>: A virtual SetRange method has been added for defining UI control ranges, enabling flexible parameter range customization.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>imorpher.h</em></strong>: Established interface classes for Morpher modifiers, expanding morphing capabilities with multiple channels of geometric transformation control.</span></li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><span style="text-indent: -18pt;"><strong><em>control.h</em></strong>: Implemented the GetDefaultController method to select appropriate user controls based on parameter types, ensuring efficient and accurate UI element assignment.</span></li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoNormal">Now that you have seen some SDK changes in 2025, let&#39;s see how you would <em>port a 2024 sample to work with 3ds Max 2025</em>.</p>
<h2>Porting the Explode Geometry Sample</h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">The Explode Geometry Sample is one of the sample plugins maintained by the <a href="https://aps.autodesk.com/adn" rel="noopener" target="_blank">ADN team</a>, with the installer available on the <a href="https://apps.autodesk.com/3DSMAX/en/Detail/Index?id=2091841125298582567&amp;appLang=en&amp;os=Win64" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Autodesk App Store</a> and the source code hosted on the <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech" rel="noopener" target="_blank">ADN GitHub repo</a>. To begin the porting process, let&#39;s begin with fetching the code we will be working with.</p>
<h3>Fetching the source code</h3>
<p class="MsoNormal">Using your favorite tool, whether<em> GitHub Desktop, SourceTree, the command line</em>, etc., clone the Explode Geometry Sample. Note that you need to clone on the version tag indicated below, as the code has been updated already to support newer versions of 3ds Max.</p>
<p><code>// Lets fetch code from v2.6 tag which supports 3ds Max 2024</code></p>
<p><code>// <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry/releases/tag/v2.6" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry/releases/tag/v2.6</a></code></p>
<p><code>git clone --branch v2.6 https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry.git</code></p>
<p><code>cd 3dsMax-Explode-Geometry</code></p>
<h3>Updating to 2025 Assembly Versions</h3>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">First, let&#39;s start by updating the assembly reference version to 3ds Max 2025 as well as setting our assembly output directory to 2025. In the <strong><em><u>.csproj</u></em></strong> project file, update the occurrence of 2024 to 2025, the assumption here being that you already have the 3ds Max 2025 setup installed.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">With the project version updated, another interesting section to update is in our `<em><code>AssemblyInfo.cs</code></em>` file. Here we have pre-defined assembly versions and other organizational details, which may need to be bumped up to match the 3ds Max 2025 version.</p>
<p><code>// Update the following two lines if need be</code><br /><code>[assembly: AssemblyVersion(&quot;2.7.0.0&quot;)]</code><br /><code>[assembly: AssemblyFileVersion(&quot;2.7.0.0&quot;)]</code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">At this point, we have all versioning details updated and ready to work on 2025 feature changes. First, let&#39;s look at our core functionality.</p>
</div>
<blockquote>
<p class="MsoNormal">Note: The system requirements for .NET are v4.8, if you have any build issues with version incompatibility, switch to v4.8.1.</p>
</blockquote>
<h3>MNVert Changes</h3>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">As noted earlier about some small changes to the C++ API that affect .NET-generated code, MNVert is among the victims of performance optimization. With the C++ API dropping the original copy operator for the C++ default copy, making MNVert trivially copiable and allocatable. This subtle change that works the same on the C++ side results in missing the `<em>Assign</em>` operator on the .NET `MNVert`.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">Below is the final output for the 2024 vs. 2025 `<em>ExplodeGeometry</em>` with the MNVert functionality unchanged. You will note that the 2025 version shows no shapes on the scene as the Assign method is missing, which assigns vertex points to the `<em>polyNewFace</em>` which we are using to create new faces.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3d487a7200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image001" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02c8d3d487a7200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3d487a7200c-800wi" title="Image001" /></a></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">&#0160;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">How can we remedy this? A quick fix is as shown below:</p>
<p><code>// Original code ..</code></p>
<p><code>polyNewFace.Mesh.V(k).Assign(vert);</code></p>
<p><code>// New code ...</code></p>
<p><code>polyNewFace.Mesh.V(k).P = vert.P;</code></p>
<p><code></code></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">Note that the method `<strong><em>Assign</em></strong>` still works on the `<em>MNVert</em>`, but this originates from the `FlagUser`, where `MNVert` derives from.</p>
</blockquote>
<p class="MsoNormal">With that fixed, let&#39;s have a look at the menu system changes and how to effect those changes in our sample.</p>
<h3>Upgrading to the new Menu System</h3>
<p class="MsoNormal">Unfortunately, we will go over all the menu changes and how to make use of them here, but you can find a detailed guide on the following topic below:</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal">The Menu System: <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=GUID-FF48D0EC-6669-4EC7-AB43-E9998A14A198">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=GUID-FF48D0EC-6669-4EC7-AB43-E9998A14A198</a> &amp; <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=menu_system">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=menu_system</a></li>
<li class="MsoNormal">Menu Migration Guide: <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=menu_migration_guide" style="text-indent: -18pt;">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=menu_migration_guide</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoListParagraphCxSpLast">&#0160;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">The sample packs a few useful packaging scripts and configuration files. This is where we will be modifying to set up the menu changes. But first, why do we need to make use of the menu in this sample?</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">The sample is distributed as part of the ADN samples through the Autodesk AppStore. As such, to invoke the sample:</p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoNormal"><em>First, the assembly must be loaded to 3ds Max, which we are achieving by using the `PackageContents.xml` file. You can check the section on ` Packaging Your Project` in the Menu Migration Guide linked above.</em></li>
<li class="MsoNormal"><em>Secondly, we expose the action items through MacroScript. This is not necessary, as we can make use of the Action table IDs directly to invoke the .NET methods.</em></li>
<li class="MsoNormal"><em>Lastly, we create a menu entry under the `<code>App Store</code>` menu item on the main menu bar.</em></li>
</ul>
<p class="MsoNormal">With all that in mind, let&#39;s navigate to the `<em><code>PackageContents.xml</code></em>` located in the `<em><code>/Bundle2</code></em>` directory and start the packaging process upgrade.</p>
<h4>PackageContents.xml file</h4>
<p class="MsoNormal">First, let&#39;s expand the package runtime environment to support 2025. This can be done by updating the `<em><code>SeriesMax</code></em>` value to 2025. Similarly, let&#39;s expand the `<em><code>SeriesMax</code></em>` for `<em><code>macroscripts parts</code></em>` segment as shown below:</p>
<p><code>&lt;RuntimeRequirements</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;OS=&quot;Win64&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;Platform=&quot;3ds Max&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;SeriesMin=&quot;2020&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;SeriesMax=&quot;2025&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>/&gt;</code></p>
<p><code>&lt;Components Description=&quot;macroscripts parts&quot;&gt;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;RuntimeRequirements ... SeriesMax=&quot;2025&quot; /&gt;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;...</code></p>
<p><code>&lt;/Components&gt;</code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">With MacroScript support for 2025 added, let&#39;s add .NET assembly as shown below.</p>
<p><code>&lt;Components Description=&quot;assemblies parts&quot;&gt;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;RuntimeRequirements OS=&quot;Win64&quot; Platform=&quot;3ds Max&quot; SeriesMin=&quot;2025&quot; SeriesMax=&quot;2025&quot; /&gt;</code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;ComponentEntry AppName=&quot;ADNExplodeGeometry&quot; Version=&quot;2.6.0&quot; ModuleName=&quot;./Contents/ManagedAssemblies/2025/ADNExplodeGeometry.dll&quot; AppDescription=&quot;...&quot; /&gt;</code><br /><code>&lt;/Components&gt;</code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;">Lastly, let&#39;s add a post-startup script for 2025 that will create the menu entry for us on 3ds Max boot. Don&#39;t worry for now; we&#39;ll create the actual file and its contents next.</p>
<p><code>&lt;Components Description=&quot;post-start-up scripts parts&quot;&gt;</code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;RuntimeRequirements OS=&quot;Win64&quot; Platform=&quot;3ds Max&quot; SeriesMin=&quot;2025&quot; SeriesMax=&quot;2025&quot; /&gt;</code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&lt;ComponentEntry AppName=&quot;ADNExplodeGeometry&quot; Version=&quot;2.6.0&quot; ModuleName=&quot;./Contents/Post-Start-Up_Scripts/ADNGeometryExplodeSetupMenu2025.ms&quot; AppDescription=&quot;Setup Menu to execute tool&quot; /&gt;</code><br /><code>&lt;/Components&gt;&#0160;</code><code></code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">&#0160;</span></p>
<h4>Creating Menu Entries for 2025</h4>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">As we noted above in the `PackageContents.xml`, we need to add a new post-startup script that will handle menu creation for our package when it&#39;s loaded. We create a new file called ` <em>ADNGeometryExplodeSetupMenu2025.ms</em>` in the <em>`./Bundle2/Contents/Post-Start-Up_Scripts/</em>` directory. Unlike 3ds Max 2024 and earlier versions, 2025 uses callbacks to register new menu entries for both regular and quad menus.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">Within the file, let&#39;s add code to register our callback as well as get the main menu bar handle, which we will use to add new menu or sub-menu entries.</span></p>
<p><code>function menuCallback = (</code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;local menuMgr = callbacks.notificationParam()</code><br /><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;local mainMenuBar = menuMgr.mainMenuBar</code><br /><code>)</code></p>
<p><code>-- Register Callback to the #CuiRegisterMenus</code><br /><code>callbacks.removeScripts id:#adnExplodeGeomMenu</code><br /><code>callbacks.addScript #cuiRegisterMenus menuCallback id:#adnExplodeGeomMenu</code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;, sans-serif;">From the callback, we can access the menu manager, which hosts the main menu bar. We&#39;ll use the main menu bar to add a sub-menu item, which will have our menu item. Let&#39;s see how this is attained:</span></p>
<p><code>local stringAppStoreDefaultMenu = &quot;App Store&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>-- ADN Explode Geometry MXS</code><br /><code>local stringMacroScriptName = &quot;ADNExplodeGeomMS&quot;</code><br /><code>local stringMacroScriptCategory = &quot;ADN Samples&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>local helpMenuId = &quot;cee8f758-2199-411b-81e7-d3ff4a80d143&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>-- ID of the &quot;App Store&quot; menu in the menu bar. Use this ID when in need of adding new submenu items</code><br /><code>-- to the &quot;App Store&quot; menu entry.</code><br /><code>local appStoreMenuId = &quot;CC18FEFC-E8A4-4B16-B519-664E8FA3B549&quot;</code></p>
<p><code>local newSubMenu = mainMenuBar.CreateSubMenu appStoreMenuId stringAppStoreDefaultMenu beforeId:helpMenuId</code></p>
<p><code>local separatorId = &quot;96FB49D4-6263-4D8E-AC95-6D304673327B&quot;</code><br /><code>newSubMenu.CreateSeparator separatorId</code></p>
<p><code>local permanentId = stringMacroScriptName + &quot;`&quot; + stringMacroScriptCategory</code></p>
<p><code>-- 647394: MacroScript Action Table ID</code><br /><code>newSubMenu.CreateAction &quot;9DE5BDB9-E47F-4614-BDF8-C331B9B38C70&quot; 647394 permanentId</code></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="border: none; padding: 0cm;"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;, sans-serif;">This script defines some local variables like the menu entry name and our menu name, as well as some system data like the `</span><strong style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;, sans-serif;"><em>Help Menu</em></strong><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;, sans-serif;">` GUUID. From the main menu bar, we create a submenu called `App Store` using </span><code><em style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;, sans-serif;">mainMenuBar.CreateSubMenu‚Å£. </em></code><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;, sans-serif;">In the submenu, we add a separator at the end of the existing menu items, if any (in our case it may be empty), and then we create a new action entry for our sample.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">With the script completed, we have one last piece remaining: adding the built assembly to the package.</span></p>
<h3>Build &amp; Adding Assembly to the Package</h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">Under the `<code><em>PackageContents.xml</em></code>` section, we added a reference to a built assembly supporting 2025. From our upgraded project, we build our project, and the generated assembly is written out to our project&#39;s <em>`OutputPath</em>` directive. We can copy over this assembly to the <em>`<code>./Bundle2/Contents/ManagedAssemblies/2025/</code>`</em> directory.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">The Bundle2 directory can be copied over as is now to the 3ds Max plugin directory, and on the next 3ds Max boot, the plugin will be loaded. For a full guide to plugin packaging, check the docs here: </span><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=packaging_plugins"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=packaging_plugins</span></a><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">.</span></p>
<h3>Final touches</h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: &#39;Aptos Display&#39;,sans-serif;">To finalize the plugin details, we can do a couple of things:</span></p>
<ul>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst">&#0160;Update version information for the plugin, as encompassed in the `<em><code>PackageContents.xml</code></em>`</li>
<li class="MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst"><em>Documentation</em>: Updating the documentation details for new features, fixes, and/or new version information.</li>
</ul>
<p>We hope you found that helpful!</p>

AUTHOR: Allan K. Koech
AUTHOR EMAIL: allan.koech@autodesk.com
TITLE: Upgrading 3ds Max .NET Projects from .NET Framework to .NET 8
STATUS: Draft
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: upgrading-3dsmax-projects-from-net-framework-to-net
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: Samples
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2025/02/upgrading-3dsmax-projects-from-net-framework-to-net.html 
DATE: 02/20/2025 07:39:37 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>3ds Max 2025 and earlier versions have used the .NET Framework for building plugins, but, with the VFX world transitioning to .NET, 3ds Max 2026 brings this support with it. As such, .NET projects require a bit of housekeeping to get them compiled and working in .NET 8 for our case. This blog is a simple walkthrough of the upgrade process, using the public <strong><em>Explode Geometry</em></strong> Sample hosted on our <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry">ADN GitHub Repo</a>.</p>
<h2><strong><span style="font-size: 14pt;">The Upgrade Assistant</span></strong></h2>
<p>Microsoft provides a Upgrade Assistant extension to help with porting .NET Framework projects to .NET as well as .NET Core to .NET and much more. The tool simplifies and aids in handling the upgrade intricacies, leaving just a few more steps for us to complete.</p>
<p>First, to get things going, check if you have the Upgrade Assistant installed. If not installed, the <strong><em>Visual Studio Extensions Manager</em> </strong>should be your first stop. With Visual Studio opened, navigate to <code>Menu &gt; Extensions &gt; Manage Extensions &gt; Under the Extensions Manager</code>, search for <code>&#39;Upgrade Assistant&#39;</code> and get it installed as shown below.</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3cc7388200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Install-upgrade-assistant" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02c8d3cc7388200c img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3cc7388200c-800wi" title="Install-upgrade-assistant" /></a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>With the assistant downloaded, follow the instructions to get it installed. This may include having to restart the IDE to get the extension installed and loaded for use.</p>
<p>Please note that the Upgrade Assistant is available as both a Visual Studio extension as well as a command-line utility. In this blog, we will only cover using the Visual Studio extension.</p>
<h2>Explode Geometry Project .NET Upgrade</h2>
<p>Let&#39;s work with our [ADN Explode Geometry Sample] (GitHub link) available on GitHub and see how we can get it building and running in .NET 8.</p>
<h3>Fetching the project</h3>
<p>This is an easy step, clone the repo (SSH, HTTPS, ZIP, or any format you prefer). Note that our GitHub repo is already updated, so fetch the older tagged version for the 2025 code for the sample.</p>
<p><code>git clone &lt;repo&gt;</code></p>
<p><code>cd &lt;repo&gt;</code></p>
<p>In the Source folder, open the <code>.csproj</code> in Visual Studio.</p>
<h3>Upgrading to .NET the Assistant-way</h3>
<p>As detailed in the Microsoft blog on the assistant, we can upgrade by <code>Right Clicking the project &gt; Upgrade &gt; A new project upgrade page is opened</code>.</p>
<p>Here, we select the project upgrade way and work with the <strong><em>in-place project upgrade,</em></strong> but feel free to test the other options if they suit your needs.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860fa1cfd200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="2.select-net-version" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e860fa1cfd200d image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860fa1cfd200d-800wi" title="2.select-net-version" /></a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>With the upgrade type ironed out, next we need to select the .NET version to upgrade to. For our case, we are going for <strong><em>.NET 8.0 LTS;</em></strong> this is the expectation for 3ds Max 2026 .NET plugins. You may optionally get an action requirement to download and install <em>.NET SDK</em> if you don&#39;t have it yet; if so, proceed with that installation, then pick it up from here once done.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3cc7439200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="3.net-version" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02c8d3cc7439200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3cc7439200c-800wi" title="3.net-version" /></a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>In the next step, we are required to select the files to upgrade. By default, all files in the project are checked, including the project file. Let&#39;s leave it as is and proceed with upgrading the selection. After the process completes, if no errors come up, then our project will have been transformed. Probably, the project will try to build but fail; we will fix that shortly. To check the logs, switch the combo box as shown below to the Upgrade Assistant option.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860e315a6200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="4.upgrade-complete" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e860e315a6200b img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860e315a6200b-800wi" title="4.upgrade-complete" /></a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>At the end of this process, you should have a project file <code>`.csproj`</code> that has been updated to conform to the .NET 8 project format. Running the build fails due to missing references to the Autodesk assemblies that may have been dropped in the upgrade process. Don&#39;t worry; fixing this is easy!</p>
<p>To fix the missing Autodesk assemblies or any other internal or 3rd party assemblies, we can achieve that either by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Directly edit the <code>csproj</code> file by copying the <em>ItemGroup</em> for the assemblies from the old project file and updating where necessary. For instance, for the Autodesk.Max.dll assembly, we can have it included in the new project file as shown below, with the version updated to 2026, of course. The same will be done for the other project dependencies like <code>CSharpUtilities.dll, ManagedServices.dll</code>, etc.</li>
</ul>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>&lt;ItemGroup&gt; </code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 80px;"><code>&lt;Reference Include=&quot;Autodesk.Max&quot;&gt; </code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 80px;"><code>&lt;HintPath&gt;$(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2026)\Autodesk.Max.dll&lt;/HintPath&gt; </code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 80px;"><code>&lt;/Reference&gt; .... other assemblies </code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>&lt;/ItemGroup&gt;</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Another way is making use of the Visual Studio Reference Manager that is accessed from the <strong><code>Menu &gt; Project &gt; Add Project Reference &gt; Browse</code></strong> &amp; find your assemblies. Once all intended libraries are selected, click OK to add them. Just as in the option above, the new assemblies will be added back into the project file. Just FYI, we can change the assembly paths for the Autodesk assemblies to make use of the path variables. This way, any user can use our plugin despite the installation path they chose. For our case, we will use the path as<strong><em> $(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2026)\&lt;assembly name&gt;</em></strong>.&#0160;</li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160; <a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860e315c3200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="5.add-asm-reference" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02e860e315c3200b img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02e860e315c3200b-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="5.add-asm-reference" /></a></p>
<p>At this stage, we can build our project, and everything should now be okay. But, looking at the logs, our build outputs are going to the default Visual Studio project build directory and not the one defined under our <strong><em>debug/release</em></strong> property group. In .NET Framework project configuration, we had defined <strong><em>&lt;OutputPath&gt;</em></strong> inside each build type (<em>Build/Debug</em>), in .NET, we define it inside the first global <em>&lt;PropertyGroup&gt;</em> where we have our project defaults as shown below;</p>
<p><code>&lt;PropertyGroup&gt;</code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>&lt;TargetFramework&gt;net8.0-windows&lt;/TargetFramework&gt;&#0160;&#0160;</code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>... the other config here </code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><strong><code>&lt;OutputPath&gt;C:\Our\intended\path\for\the\assembly&lt;/OutputPath&gt;&#0160;</code></strong></p>
<p><code>&lt;/PropertyGroup&gt;</code></p>
<p>For our case, we will be using the Autodesk plugin path as our output path. This way, any plugin development changes can be updated in the plugin directory for testing.</p>
<p><span style="color: #2d2d2d;">Note: There may be extra steps to getting the assembly loaded into 3ds Max. If using <strong><em>PackageContents.xml</em></strong>, update where necessary to get the assembly and its dependencies loaded. Refer to the following documentation pages for help: <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=menu_migration_guide">Menu System Migration</a>, <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2025/ENU/?guid=packaging_plugins">Packaging Samples</a>&#0160;</span></p>
<h3><br />Final Housekeeping&#0160;</h3>
<p>As a close, we need to do a bit of housekeeping. Here are a few things to consider:</p>
<ul>
<li>Setting included assemblies as not private: When we add assembly references in our project, the build process ends up copying the assembly references and their dependencies to the `OutputPath` directory, which is not the intended behavior. This results in duplication of assemblies, which may cause 3ds Max to crash. To resolve this, update each of the included assemblies as follows:</li>
</ul>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>&lt;Reference Include=&quot;ManagedServices&quot;&gt;&#0160;</code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 80px;"><code>&lt;HintPath&gt; $(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2026)\ManagedServices.dll &lt;/HintPath&gt;&#0160;&#0160;</code></p>
<p style="padding-left: 80px;"><strong><code>&lt;Private&gt; false &lt;/Private&gt;&#0160;</code></strong></p>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>&lt;/Reference&gt;&#0160;</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Disabling <code>&#0160;AppendTargetFrameworkToOutputPath</code>&#0160;flag: Since plugins for 3ds Max are meant for Windows, we can disable the flag above to ensure the assemblies don&#39;t end up nested in a target framework directory.&#0160;</li>
</ul>
<p style="padding-left: 40px;"><code>&lt;AppendTargetFrameworkToOutputPath&gt; false &lt;/AppendTargetFrameworkToOutputPath&gt;</code></p>
<ul>
<li>Updating/bumping up plugin versions. This applies to both ApplicationVersion and AssemblyVersion</li>
</ul>
<p><br />What did I miss out on? Please let us know! Happy upgrading :smile:!</p>
-----

TITLE: Saving QWidget Docking States per 3ds Max Scene
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: saving-qwidget-docking-states-per-3ds-max-scene
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: qt
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2024/01/saving-qwidget-docking-states-per-3ds-max-scene.html 
DATE: 01/25/2024 10:33:05 AM
-----
BODY:
<p><strong> <a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3a92bf8200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, &#39;_blank&#39;, &#39;width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0&#39; ); return false"><img alt="Cover" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02c8d3a92bf8200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02c8d3a92bf8200b-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="Cover" /></a><br /></strong></p>
<h2>The Flexibility of Docking Windows</h2>
<p>Within 3ds Max, windows and panels can either float freely or be docked onto another panel, providing a customizable layout tailored to the user&#39;s preferences. This flexibility proves vital, especially considering the diverse screen sizes and DPI configurations prevalent today. Ensuring our tools are strategically positioned enhances the user experience without compromising the workspace.</p>
<p>Docking isn&#39;t confined to native Win32 UI elements; 3ds Max supports the creation of custom tools (plugins) using Qt for the UI. This empowers developers to build robust tools that seamlessly align with their workflow. Even commercial tools can be crafted with the flexibility of docking to existing UI elements.</p>
<h2>Crafting a Dockable Widget in Qt</h2>
<p>To create a dockable widget in Qt for 3ds Max, we typically derive a widget class from <strong><em>QDockWidget</em></strong>. In the context of 3ds Max plugin development, the <em><strong>QMaxDockWidget</strong></em>&#0160;offers enhanced control and integration with the 3ds Max UI elements. The SDK provides a variety of UI elements, accessible in the <em>&lt;sdk installation path/include/qt/&gt;</em>&#0160;directory.</p>
<p>Here is an example:</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><code>// Code Excerpt</code></p>
<p><code>class ADNSampleQmaxDocking</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;: public UtilityObj, </code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; public MaxSDK::QmaxDockWidget </code></p>
<p><code>{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; // ... other member functions</code></p>
<p><code>public slots:</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;void onTopLevelChanged(bool isFloating);</code></p>
<p><code>private:</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;void LoadSavedLayout(); // To load saved layouts</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;// ... other member variables</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;QString m_layoutPath;</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;MaxSDK::QmaxMainWindow* qmaxMainWindow; // Save a reference to the Qt MainWindow</code></p>
<p><code>};</code></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The code skeleton above outlines the necessary structure for creating a dockable Qt widget for a UtilityObj-derived plugin. Remember that, as a UtilityObj plugin, additional functions must be implemented. Our constructor initializes the dock widget and sets the QSettings saving path.</p>
<p>Below is an excerpt from the constructor:</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><code>// Code Excerpt</code></p>
<p><code>ADNSampleQmaxDocking::ADNSampleQmaxDocking(MaxSDK::QmaxMainWindow* parent)</code></p>
<p><code>: iu(nullptr), QmaxDockWidget(parent)</code></p>
<p><code>{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; // ... other initialization</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; // Set the desired directory</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;MSTR path = GetCOREInterface()-&gt;GetDir(APP_SCENE_DIR); </code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; path.append(_M(&quot;\\dockslayout.ini&quot;));</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; // ... other setup</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;m_layoutPath = QString::fromWCharArray(path);</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; show();</code></p>
<p><code>}</code></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The constructor establishes the default dock position, sets the desired save directory (we have used the scene directory in this example), and creates a filename for the<strong><em> .ini</em></strong> settings file. To load the layout after initialization, we implement the `<strong><em>BeginEditParams</em></strong>` function:</p>
<p><code>// Code Excerpt</code></p>
<p><code>void ADNSampleQmaxDocking::BeginEditParams(Interface* ip, IUtil* iu)</code></p>
<p><code>{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;// ... initialization and adding plugin widgets</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;// Load the saved scene layout file if it already exists</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;LoadSavedLayout();</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;// Connect topLevelChanged for the dock window to the saving of the layout</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;connect(this, &amp;MaxSDK::QmaxDockWidget::topLevelChanged, </code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; this, &amp;ADNSampleQmaxDocking::onTopLevelChanged);</code></p>
<p><code>}</code></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>We connect the `<strong><em>topLevelChanged</em></strong>` signal, saving the new layout only when the window is docked. The two slots, `<strong><em>onTopLevelChanged</em></strong>` and `<strong><em>LoadSavedLayout</em></strong>`, complete the setup as shown below.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><code>// Code Excerpt</code></p>
<p><code>void ADNSampleQmaxDocking::onTopLevelChanged(bool isFloating)</code></p>
<p><code>{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; // Save on docking state</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; // The isFloating flag can be used to save the docks when not floating</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160; qmaxMainWindow-&gt;saveLayout(m_layoutPath);</code></p>
<p><code>}</code></p>
<p><code>void ADNSampleQmaxDocking::LoadSavedLayout()</code></p>
<p><code>{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;try</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; qmaxMainWindow-&gt;loadLayout(m_layoutPath);</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;}</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;catch ()</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;{</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; &#0160;&#0160; // Handle errors</code></p>
<p><code>&#0160; &#0160;&#0160;}</code></p>
<p><code>}</code></p>
<p>Executing the application and starting the plugin will create the <strong><em>.ini</em></strong> file in the selected directory if it doesn&#39;t exist. This file saves not only the single plugin but all widgets and toolbars in use, restoring them if they are already open.</p>
<h2>Leveraging Qt in 3DS Max</h2>
<p>In conclusion, when building UI in Qt for 3ds Max, utilizing Qt tools already integrated into the software provides an elegant solution for saving and restoring docking states. Further optimizations and adjustments can be made to meet specific needs. The full code is attached below as a <strong><em>.zip</em></strong> file; feel free to explore and share your thoughts on this functionality.</p>
<p>Happy coding! Cheers!<br /><br />Full project source code:&#0160;<span class="asset  asset-generic at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02c8d3a99401200d img-responsive"><a href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/files/adndockingsample.zip">Download ADNDockingSample&#0160;</a><br /><br /></span></p>

TITLE: Porting MaxPlus to pymxs - What you need to know
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: porting-maxplus-to-pymxs-what-you-need-to-know-1
CATEGORY: MAXScript
CATEGORY: Python
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2023/06/porting-maxplus-to-pymxs-what-you-need-to-know-1.html 
DATE: 06/12/2023 03:55:36 AM
-----
BODY:
<p></p>
<article class="page sans" id="f11023ef-a477-4744-830f-076c9fab7daf"><header><img class="page-cover-image" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/maxplus2pymxs/pymxs.jpeg" style="object-position: center 40.910000000000004%;" />
<h1 class="page-title">Porting MaxPlus to pymxs - What you need to know</h1>
</header>
<div class="page-body">
<h2 class="" id="eb0624c4-0711-40a4-9fdb-67526cf4b178">Introduction</h2>
<p class="" id="3d7a8b95-605e-4da0-a034-0ca988b6b51c">As of 3ds Max 2022, the MaxPlus library is deprecated. This blog intends to assist those using MaxPlus to transition to pymxs for 3ds Max. This article will focus on an example of porting the xref system from MaxPlus to pymxs.</p>
<blockquote class="" id="5f02ef64-f404-4751-847b-d58cd10ec687">As of 3ds Max 2021, MaxPlus was not supported in Python 3. From 3ds Max 2022, shipping of MaxPlus stopped as <em><strong>pymxs </strong></em>became the supported Python scripting in 3ds Max. Check here for complete documentation <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=MAXDEV_Python_what_s_new_in_3ds_max_python_api_html">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=MAXDEV_Python_what_s_new_in_3ds_max_python_api_html</a>.</blockquote>
<h2 class="" id="1d139731-16d1-4063-977f-d8cda773e24b">3ds Max Scripting</h2>
<p class="" id="166fd311-5fa2-490f-8855-711600aa9e5c">Scripting in 3ds Max has been a powerful tool for automating tasks and creating custom plugins that extend the functionality offered by 3ds Max or introduce new features not present in the software. This capability is crucial in Design Automation, where activities are executed within the Autodesk Platform Services (formerly known as Forge). To harness the power of scripting, 3ds Max provides two primary options: MAXScript, the native scripting language of 3ds Max, and Python, a wrapper around MAXScript. By leveraging these scripting languages, users can achieve high flexibility and control over 3ds Max. Additionally, 3ds Max offers SDKs for C++ and C# for those who prefer plugin development, allowing for the creation and extension of capabilities within the software.</p>
<h2 class="" id="480adc8b-c42d-48d0-a363-33960cccf035">Scripting in MAXScript</h2>
<p class="" id="1ed15d25-2b24-4a9f-8e69-714567ec5ecb">MAXScript comes baked into 3ds Max by default and is accessible o the bottom left window of the UI or through the Scripting menu option in 3ds Max.</p>
<figure class="image" id="70908664-7a7c-4a7a-902c-b52187e54750"><a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/maxplus2pymxs/Untitled.png"><img src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/maxplus2pymxs/Untitled.png" style="width: 480px;" /></a>
<figcaption>Scripting menu option in 3ds Max 2023</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="" id="4076922d-144c-462b-83b1-74d68ecfe512">For instance, click the Scripting Listener option on the drop-down above to launch the scripting window. This brings a Scripting listener window with two choices of MAXScript and Python. Scripts can be inputted and executed in the editor window when we move to a new line, as shown below.</p>
<figure class="image" id="760f866e-3c92-4620-a5f4-964deed99595" style="text-align: center;"><a href="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/maxplus2pymxs/Untitled 1.png"><img src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/maxplus2pymxs/Untitled 1.png" style="width: 528px;" /></a>
<figcaption>MAXScript listener window showing script execution</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="" id="9a26afda-27ee-4ea9-b32c-4bec84d1d329">To learn more on how to use MAXScript and its complete tools, look at the documentation here <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=GUID-F039181A-C072-4469-A329-AE60FF7535E7">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=GUID-F039181A-C072-4469-A329-AE60FF7535E7</a>.</p>
<h2 class="" id="d314158e-cb82-46a4-a492-396ed787fced">Scripting in Python</h2>
<p class="" id="d3333ec9-208b-4acb-bfbf-2eced02a685a">Scripting in Python has been an option for quite some time now. Initially, 3ds Max exposed its APIs through a library called MaxPlus (<a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__developer_maxplus_python_api_introduction_maxplus_python_api_main_classes_html">https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__developer_maxplus_python_api_introduction_maxplus_python_api_main_classes_html</a>) which became deprecated in 3ds Max 2019 and was replaced by pymxs. Both libraries work differently and have differences in functionalities that get exposed to Python.</p>
<p class="" id="26110592-e3c2-42a4-8a1a-30a90036f7c1">To compare the difference, the code below shows how the code structure looks to create an object on scene and modify its parameters.</p>
<pre class="code" id="98389666-c9a6-48c5-bd4b-5746a4b61195"><code>import MaxPlus

obj = MaxPlus.Factory.CreateGeomObject(MaxPlus.ClassIds.Box)
obj.ParameterBlock.Width.Value = 10.0
obj.ParameterBlock.Length.Value = 10.0
obj.ParameterBlock.Height.Value = 10.0</code></pre>
<p class="" id="1c0b42e1-d543-42e0-9166-0e62617b9db4">&#0160;</p>
<pre class="code code-wrap" id="6145d614-13f8-49a1-8c63-6aa2b1757b44"><code>import pymxs

obj = pymxs.runtime.box(width=10.0, length=10.0, height=10.0)
</code></pre>
<p class="" id="416c418f-e111-4ba3-97a7-3f11124fae7c">&#0160;</p>
<h3 class="" id="f2dccbbc-e62d-4ba3-ad1e-2e75a674390e">Why the difference?</h3>
<p class="" id="078a2447-1e57-4a8d-80aa-7a134f85bf19">If you are familiar with 3ds Max SDK, the MaxPlus code has a similar approach when creating objects. It‚Äôs generated from the C++ SDK, so its code system follows how it‚Äôs done in C++ or in .NET.</p>
<p class="" id="81efde74-ba1a-42a6-bf64-701e6834066c">Unlike MaxPlus, pymxs, on the other hand, follows a different approach. Notice the first code we did for MAXScript to add a box to the scene, similar - right? Pymxs is built as a wrapper around MAXScript rather than the C++ SDK. As such, the code looks more straightforward to understand if you know bits of scripting in MAXScript.</p>
<h2 class="" id="392199a6-4ebe-4577-9f22-2848a13b7a74">Porting MaxPlus to pymxs</h2>
<p class="" id="dadc3274-c20b-4975-96b9-0f0094a06183">Let‚Äôs say you have some old scripts you made in MaxPlus, and you want to port them over to the recent version of 3ds Max, but now, the latest 3ds Max versions no longer ship MaxPlus libraries. The option is porting the codebase to either C++/.NET, MAXScript or Python. Let‚Äôs look at some examples:</p>
<h3 class="" id="64b6c992-3175-463f-b296-1a7086db2b19">1. XREFS</h3>
<p class="" id="8640453c-ec1e-41cf-9305-35bde2726764">xrefs is a terminology for external referencing other files or scenes in the current scene. This prevents loading whole exterior projects into the current project but instead just referencing it. MaxPlus provides direct manipulation of xref files as follows:</p>
<p class="" id="1f356d4e-2505-4029-9782-4ba6531c28a7">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="9e896b68-86fb-43bb-9179-712f668b1106"><mark class="highlight-brown"><span data-darkreader-inline-border-bottom="" style="border-bottom: 0.05em solid;"><em><strong>File counting</strong></em></span></mark></p>
<pre class="code code-wrap" id="01f3697d-2132-4769-8001-b0800ce19e99"><code>import MaxPlus

num_xrefs = MaxPlus.XRefs.GetXRefFileCount()
print(num_xrefs)
</code></pre>
<p class="" id="2024bb24-228e-46f6-a5d4-1847f12741c9">An equivalent pymxs code for a similar functionality is given below</p>
<pre class="code" id="4c37d7a3-e501-4bc7-a883-50dbe0f5b2ec"><code>import pymxs
num_xrefs = pymxs.runtime.xrefs.getXRefFileCount()
print(num_xrefs)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="6247abf1-9fbe-4542-ae96-41f252e64101">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="ef5cf411-0224-431a-b7c0-f0f5fdd6d537"><mark class="highlight-brown"><span data-darkreader-inline-border-bottom="" style="border-bottom: 0.05em solid;"><em><strong>Getting xref file</strong></em></span></mark></p>
<p class="" id="4d0c1a54-b6b8-4e76-9d7c-e917f1020520">Once xrefs are created within a scene, retrieving specific xref files for any purpose can be achieved as follows in both MaxPlus and pymxs</p>
<pre class="code" id="82e12b72-e5d6-48b4-979d-fd17cf7aa56c"><code>import MaxPlus

index = 0 # index of the xref file
xref_file = MaxPlus.XRefs.GetXRefFile(index)
print(xref_file)

# IN PYMXS

import pymxs

index = 0 # index of the xref file
xref_file = pymxs.runtime.xrefs.getXRefFile(index)
print(xref_file)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="26b5750d-312e-4f0e-a44d-6bc71e4914b1">Note that both require a parameter specifying the index of the XRef file to get information about.</p>
<p class="" id="6202077d-7af0-4426-a101-2dd33069affd">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="676ed381-e1b2-429f-8cb7-401cb36349e3"><mark class="highlight-brown"><span data-darkreader-inline-border-bottom="" style="border-bottom: 0.05em solid;"><em><strong> Setting xref file</strong></em></span></mark></p>
<p class="" id="41572908-3918-4bb8-a35c-f286dec3a010">This is intended for setting a file to xref</p>
<pre class="code code-wrap" id="bbfbc9c5-8076-4338-8877-239b2beef5c5"><code>import MaxPlus

# get the XRef object that you want to set the file path for
xref_object = MaxPlus.Core.GetINodeByName(&quot;MyXRefObject&quot;)

# set the file path for the XRef object
file_path = &quot;C:/path/to/my/xref/file.max&quot;
MaxPlus.Core.SetXRefFile(xref_object, file_path)
</code></pre>
<p class="" id="0643248d-29ec-4d70-84c5-4cfe5fd41b2a">Note that this code represents a workaround for updating the XRef file since there is no direct way to update the file in pymxs.</p>
<pre class="code" id="45d5022c-75ad-429e-94c5-3c5069fa9419"><code>import pymxs

index = 1
# Get the XRef object for index 1
xref_obj = pymxs.runtime.xrefs.getXRefFile(index)

new_file = &quot;path\to\file\something.max&quot;

# Using MAXScript in pymxs
maxscript_code = f&#39;&#39;&#39;
axref = xrefs.getXRefFile {index}
axref.filename = &quot;{new_file}&quot;
flagChanged axref
&#39;&#39;&#39;

_axref = pymxs.runtime.execute(maxscript_code)

print(_axref)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="89027252-e918-414a-93bf-019393a88d0c">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="3bda0364-30cf-4ad6-8962-851295bbc703"><span data-darkreader-inline-border-bottom="" style="border-bottom: 0.05em solid;"><em><mark class="highlight-brown"><strong>Flagging xref file as changed</strong></mark></em></span></p>
<p class="" id="e23e62f4-8808-4b57-a02f-7e81fb7625a6">Used to flag that the xref has been changed.</p>
<pre class="code" id="a5c8f552-b57f-4010-a831-10472b592553"><code>import MaxPlus

# get the XRef object that you want to flag as changed
xref_object = MaxPlus.Core.GetINodeByName(&quot;MyXRefObject&quot;)

# flag the XRef object as changed
MaxPlus.Core.FlagXrefChanged(xref_object)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="6c8d8c6b-8c7c-4eef-b884-39256e0344d0">To flag specific file as changed, pymxs doesn‚Äôt expose any way to directly do that. Alternatively, we can invoke MAXScript to flag the files as changed as shown;</p>
<pre class="code" id="80be72d9-8dc1-44f8-8727-b27988085099"><code>import pymxs

index = 1 # Index for the xref you want to flag as updated

maxscript_code = f&#39;&#39;&#39;
axref = xrefs.getXRefFile {index}
flagChanged axref
axref
&#39;&#39;&#39;

_axref = pymxs.runtime.execute(maxscript_code)

print(_axref)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="8cc1b276-4c7e-4a2e-8baa-c569c0f8f564">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="283c1d93-03fd-4902-a28d-fc1e266aa193"><mark class="highlight-brown"><em><strong>Updating changed xrefs</strong></em></mark></p>
<p class="" id="5b0d485e-2227-488e-91e9-5c604e622af0">Updates the XRefs that have been flagged as changed. This function actually loads the new versions of the referenced files and updates the XRefs in the scene accordingly.</p>
<pre class="code" id="6a161375-79cf-40c0-8dc2-7d342ed3d29e"><code># In MAXPLUS
import MaxPlus

# update all XRef objects that have been flagged as changed
MaxPlus.Core.UpdateChangedXRefs()

# In PYMXS
import pymxs

# Updates the changed XRefs and resets their changed flags
pymxs.runtime.xrefs.updateChangedXRefs()</code></pre>
<p class="" id="96c052ee-9c2e-4c17-b141-139a46d1f7a0">&#0160;</p>
<h3 class="" id="9c6967e0-7b75-4e6c-8f46-83dc1aa04d50">3. Animation</h3>
<p class="" id="12c16d6b-f39e-4ded-af33-f7a08a8e03af"><mark class="highlight-brown"><span data-darkreader-inline-border-bottom="" style="border-bottom: 0.05em solid;"><em><strong>Getting Animation Range</strong></em></span></mark></p>
<p class="" id="f71aee48-3a0a-4ba6-9b94-27991850a1c0">Getting Animation Range is used to retrieve the animation range of the current scene.</p>
<pre class="code" id="435b0d72-f061-4f56-b46a-6d0a22e48b5c"><code>import MaxPlus

# get the animation range of the current scene
start_time, end_time = MaxPlus.Animation.GetAnimRange()

# print the start and end times of the animation range
print(&quot;Animation Range:&quot;)
print(&quot;Start Time:&quot;, start_time)
print(&quot;End Time:&quot;, end_time)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="e29b63f3-16bd-4c7e-bad8-fff29957b6d5">MaxPlus&#39;s corresponding function in pymxs returns a pair of <em>time</em> objects: the first element of the tuple is the animation range&#39;s start time, and the second element is the animation range&#39;s end time.</p>
<pre class="code" id="1144445f-cc30-453f-af86-5a3f6579e8e3"><code>import pymxs

# Get the animation range in 3ds Max
anim_range = pymxs.runtime.animationRange

# Print the start and end times of the animation range
print(&quot;Start Time:&quot;, anim_range.start)
print(&quot;End Time:&quot;, anim_range.end)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="10ba55af-e8c8-4035-b100-d5357b979165">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="ef315fe8-275d-4cd0-b8fb-9b4ff869719e"><mark class="highlight-brown"><span data-darkreader-inline-border-bottom="" style="border-bottom: 0.05em solid;"><strong><em>Getting current time</em></strong></span></mark></p>
<p class="" id="e87c7873-ea81-48c9-b43e-87243841ab07">Returns current time in the animation</p>
<pre class="code" id="17e48da5-c65e-49fa-aa00-a2a63889e1ca"><code>import MaxPlus

# get the current time in the animation
current_time = MaxPlus.Animation.GetTime()

# print the current time to the console
print(&quot;Current Time:&quot;, current_time)</code></pre>
<p class="" id="97a4c0f7-aebb-44f4-8550-8d5c004ae474">The following code samples are used to get the current time when animating in pymxs.</p>
<pre class="code" id="0e6f8658-c22b-4bd2-be22-594117b10a35"><code>import pymxs

# get current time 
current_time = pymxs.runtime.currentTime

# Log the values
print(current_time)
print(current_time.frame)
print(current_time.ticks)</code></pre>
<h2 class="" id="0185fbc1-17d7-4c89-bc8a-fd6aa460cebd">Conclusion</h2>
<p class="" id="12643c9b-226e-45ef-b906-4815dc9f464b">The samples do not cover all the aspects of porting code from MaxPlus to pymxs. However, the complete guide can be found on the documentation at <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=MAXDEV_Python_using_pymxs_maxplus_to_pymxs_html">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=MAXDEV_Python_using_pymxs_maxplus_to_pymxs_html</a>. The guide aimed to give ideas on how to look at porting current codes to pymxs.</p>
<p class="" id="ce730b9f-1ea7-400b-9188-d3eb49bf68a2">&#0160;</p>
<p class="" id="b5a8bcef-f1dc-45ef-9cf5-9f987a4a3b6e">We have looked at both pymxs native functions similar to or representing the MaxPlus functions and embedding MAXScript in pymxs to achieve functionality not currently exposed to pymxs.</p>
<p class="" id="63cb9100-d4f7-4cb2-a9b2-ce34885a0271">&#0160;</p>
<h2 class="" id="0ab5ffc8-b5ef-41a4-94b8-10e749d1af4d">FAQ‚Äôs</h2>
<ul class="toggle" id="22de1069-6214-4a03-bf75-cdd6cb73747f">
<li><details open="">
<summary>Are MaxPlus and pymxs one-to-one match?</summary>
<p class="" id="fc4b9914-7590-4f01-87e7-50264f0e070d">No. Due to the architecture, these two bear different exposure to underlying functionalities. So, some functions and modules in MaxPlus are not available in pymxs and vice versa.</p>
</details></li>
</ul>
<ul class="toggle" id="dbabe610-1250-48bb-8aff-27cc05697188">
<li><details open="">
<summary>Can I convert my MaxPlus code to pymxs fully?</summary>
<p class="" id="d9554def-bf7c-442b-ac45-69df53558959">Yes. MaxPlus code can be ported to pymxs, but no one-to-one conversion exists. Note that you‚Äôll need to combine pymxs and MAXScript for some functionality to achieve it. It‚Äôs all about getting similar functionality.</p>
</details></li>
</ul>
<ul class="toggle" id="6b0c72bd-5a46-4989-b9ee-0ecc16758507">
<li><details open="">
<summary>So, what about pymxs and MAXScript?</summary>
<p class="" id="bfece71a-8e45-42a3-83d2-b8c2b6ecb3f0">pymxs is a MAXScript wrapper but not all functionality and properties in MAXScript are directly generated into pymxs modules/functions/properties. There are workarounds but not direct functions/modules like the ones in MAXScript.</p>
</details></li>
</ul>
</div>
</article>
-----

TITLE: 3ds Max 2024 Released!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: 3ds-max-2024-released

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2023/04/3ds-max-2024-released.html 
DATE: 04/06/2023 04:17:21 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02b7519e8f5c200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="2024_blog" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c02b7519e8f5c200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c02b7519e8f5c200c-800wi" title="2024_blog" /></a></p>
<p>Well, another year has passed, and another great release of 3ds Max has arrived. Check out the new features of 3ds Max 2024 <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2024/ENU/?guid=GUID-5F6E1DF3-C9E4-4784-A5C3-31C2490688D0">here</a>. <br />Changes for the 3ds Max 2024 SDK are documented <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2024_sdk">here</a>. Highlights from the SDK include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2024_sdk#sdk-break">SDK Break</a> - means you should recompile any plugins for use with 3ds Max 2024.</li>
<li>3ds Max 2024 and the SDK are now using C++17 as a standard. For bringing older plugin code into the 2024 SDK, you should consider changing the project settings to use C++17 (C/C++ -&gt; Language -&gt; C++ Language Standard) to be ISO C++17 Standard. This is especially important for newer headers and API features to be compatible. For all the details, see <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2024_sdk#c-version">here</a>. The plugin wizard and underlying property pages are already updated.</li>
<li>New <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2024_sdk#color-management-api">Color Management API</a></li>
<li><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2024_sdk#mesh-mnmesh-and-beziershape-api-changes">Mesh and MNMesh changes&#0160;</a> (Note that BezierShape is mentioned there, but it is a mistake... no changes to that class).</li>
</ul>
<p>Another change for the 2024 release is that the <a href="https://manage.autodesk.com">https://manage.autodesk.com</a> download now does not include the SDK due to size restrictions. You can get the SDK from the <a href="https://www.autodesk.com/develop3dsmax">3ds Max developer center here</a>, or from the ADN Member site. Note that we are also posting the 3ds Max USD SDK in those locations as well.</p>
<p>For all the changes to the customization environments, check out these sections:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=whats_new_3dsmax_2024_sdk">What&#39;s New: 3ds Max 2024 SDK</a></li>
<li><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=What-s-New-in-MAXScript-in-3ds">What&#39;s New in MAXScript in 3ds Max 2024</a></li>
<li><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2024/ENU/?guid=MAXDEV_Python_what_s_new_in_3ds_max_python_api_html">What&#39;s New in 3ds Max Python</a></li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>

AUTHOR: Allan K. Koech
