TITLE: Learning 3ds Max SDK - My Journey
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: markdown
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: learning-3ds-max-sdk-my-journey
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: qt
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick
CATEGORY: Training
CATEGORY: webcast
CATEGORY: Weblogs

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2023/02/learning-3ds-max-sdk-my-journey.html 
DATE: 02/03/2023 08:28:00 AM
-----
BODY:
<p><img src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/blog2/image001.png" alt="image001" />  </p>

<p><em>Image adapted from <a href="http://aneeswork.blogspot.com/2015/10/3d-interior-design-3ds-max-vray.html">http://aneeswork.blogspot.com/2015/10/3d-interior-design-3ds-max-vray.html</a></em>
<br /></p>

<h1>Learning 3ds Max SDK: My Journey</h1>

<p>One thing has always fascinated me for a very long time, that is, programming. I used to really wonder how big software did work and how they came to being. The absolute beauty of just writing English grammar with some semantics and later the computer gets to understand it, isn‚Äôt that just awesome?  </p>

<p>My journey learning 3ds Max and 3ds Max SDK was not that easy. Let‚Äôs be frank, transitioning into a new codebase, semantics, UI, documentation, etc. is overwhelming at start.  </p>

<h2>So, why learn the SDK?</h2>

<p>Let‚Äôs address the elephant in the room, the why question. It‚Äôs with no doubt if you ever used any software, you ever felt like, <strong><em>‚ÄúI wish I had this feature‚Äù</em></strong> or <strong><em>‚ÄúI wish this was simpler‚Äù</em></strong> or ‚ÄúI wish I could be able to just automate these tasks‚Äù. Yes, I know the frustration of sometimes finding out what you wanted isn‚Äôt available or is just long and tedious. We mostly solve some of such tasks with keyboard key-bindings (shortcuts) but some tasks are not that simple for such operations. That‚Äôs where the SDK comes into play. Giving you the ability to make and tweak as you wish.  </p>

<p>With access to the APIs through the SDK, you are given the power to make your own custom plugins to add or modify existing tasks, automate operations like rendering, generations, etc. and much more! But with such power comes some responsibility, let‚Äôs look at them in a bit!  </p>

<h2>Prerequisites</h2>

<p>To be able to learn 3ds Max and its SDK, you require some tools and knowledge. 
<br /></p>

<ul>
<li><strong>Programming knowledge</strong> ‚Äì Definitely this is a must. Though not a mastery of the subject but a good understanding of the basics. Of much concern here is C++ although the SDK also has .NET and Python bindings. In C++, these are some topics that you will require understanding to work well with the SDK: classes, objects, inheritance, polymorphism, virtual functions, abstract classes, pointers, references, etc.</li>
<li><strong>A good computer/laptop</strong> ‚Äì Check <a href="https://knowledge.autodesk.com/support/3ds-max/learn-explore/caas/sfdcarticles/sfdcarticles/System-requirements-for-Autodesk-3ds-Max-products.html">https://knowledge.autodesk.com/support/3ds-max/learn-explore/caas/sfdcarticles/sfdcarticles/System-requirements-for-Autodesk-3ds-Max-products.html</a> for a detailed machine requirements to be able to run 3ds Max smoothly. Depending on the version of 3ds Max you intend to run, the machine specification may be a bit different. </li>
<li><strong>Visual Studio IDE</strong> ‚Äì Though not a compulsory requirement, for a newbie it may be. The IDE will handle most setup, environment variables etc. automatically if using the plugin wizard. Programming can still be done using a normal code editor (i.e., Visual Studio Code or Notepad) and build &amp; compile done on the Command Line (CMD). Visual Studio IDE Community, Professional or Enterprise will work for this setup.</li>
<li><strong>3ds Max &amp; 3ds Max SDK</strong> ‚Äì Installation of 3ds Max and its SDK is required. Check out how to install and setup the SDK here <a href="https://knowledge.autodesk.com/support/3ds-max/troubleshooting/caas/sfdcarticles/sfdcarticles/How-to-install-the-Software-Development-Kit-SDK-for-3ds-Max.html">https://knowledge.autodesk.com/support/3ds-max/troubleshooting/caas/sfdcarticles/sfdcarticles/How-to-install-the-Software-Development-Kit-SDK-for-3ds-Max.html</a>. Also do setup the plugin wizard for easy project setup on visual studio IDE by following the instructions here <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=installing_the_plug-in_wizard_ap">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=installing_the_plug-in_wizard_ap</a>.</li>
<li><strong>Qt Knowledge</strong> ‚Äì <em>[OPTIONAL]</em> If you ever need to build plugins that will have user interactions, 3ds Max has support for adding UI based on Qt Widgets as from 3ds Max 2017. Check <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=using_qt_with_3ds_max_plug-ins">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=using_qt_with_3ds_max_plug-ins</a> for instructions of setting up Qt with Visual Studio.</li>
<li><strong><em>Patience</em></strong> ‚Äì Learning takes time, takes practice, takes iterations. Give yourself time to internalize the concepts. No one becomes a pro overnight. </li>
</ul>

<p><br />
<br /></p>

<p><em>NOTE: This is very important to note: Depending on the 3ds Max version you chose, let‚Äôs say 3ds Max 3ds Max 2023, each version supports a specific SDK version, Visual Studio compilers, Qt version, etc. Always check for the right versions from the site <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=sdk_requirements">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=sdk_requirements</a>. This gives each MAX version and the compatible OS, SDK, C++ compiler, .NET framework and Qt version.</em>  </p>

<p><br />  </p>

<h2>So where do I start?</h2>

<p>With all the pre-requisites satisfied, am sure you have a strong quest to get your feet on the move. 3ds Max is a big software, developed for decades. As such, it comes with history of then and now. Depending on the material you can get your hands on to read or watch, you may be getting old concepts that may have been deprecated or changed to new formats. Always keep that in mind. <br />
<br /></p>

<p>3ds Max introduces some new terminologies, youll get to hear things like modifiers, reference systems, parameter blocks, nodes, etc. Delving into these topics right away seems a bit overwhelming. Here is how I handled it:</p>

<ul>
<li><p><strong><em>Learn 3ds Max UI basics first</em></strong> ‚Äì To understand how things work behind the scenes, we need to know how its handled on the scene. User interaction with the software is important and most critical and a s such, knowing how to work as a user gives you knowledge of how objects are modified stack by stack till you attain a desired 3d object. The areas to start with are:</p>

<ul>
<li><strong>Basic geometric objects</strong> ‚Äì Getting to know how to create box, sphere, cylinder, etc. objects on scene. This also entails, how to modify the parameters of such objects like length, width, height, segments, etc. </li>
<li><strong>Transforms</strong> ‚Äì This is basically 3d manipulations on an object on scene. It‚Äôs applied on the entire object and its independent of the shape of the scene object. It‚Äôs the object position, rotation, and scale. </li>
<li><strong>Modifiers</strong> ‚Äì This is how the basic shapes are changed. Adding modifiers on them allows manipulation of the underlying object. For instance, adding a bend modifier on a straight object gives an output as shown below. Check out how such a modifier is added and resulting effect on the object here <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/videos/0zd2FvbTrAtMzQjiHcH39SnEZstxFDYC/video.webm">https://help.autodesk.com/videos/0zd2FvbTrAtMzQjiHcH39SnEZstxFDYC/video.webm</a>. Other types of modifiers are: Edit poly, OpenSubdiv, chamfer, shell, etc. <br />
<br />
<br />  </li>
</ul>

<p><img src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/blog2/image002.jpg" alt="image002" />  </p>

<p><br />
<br />  </p>

<ul>
<li><strong>Animation and animation controllers</strong> ‚Äì This entail adding motion to scene objects. 3ds Max comes with a couple of animation controllers that you can attach to your object on scene. The keyframe timeline allow for keyframe manipulation of the animation motion. A basic understanding of how to do animation and use the different tools on the UI for the same purpose is important to working with animation on the SDK later. Learn more here <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__interactive_help_animation_animation_controllers_html">https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=<em><em>interactive</em>help</em>animation_animation_controllers_html</a>.</li>
<li><strong>Lighting and Rendering</strong> ‚Äì After all modification on objects has been completed, we add lights to give a realistic object before it rendered out to a desired output format. This section will give insights of the different render engines and how they work, how to work with different light types, working with cameras, etc. Here is a pictorial of scene lighting. Read more on this here <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__interactive_help_lighting_rendering_html">https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=<em><em>interactive</em>help</em>lighting_rendering_html</a>. <br />
<br />
<br />  </li>
</ul>

<p><img src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/blog2/image003.jpg" alt="image003" />  </p>

<p><br />
<br />  </p>

<ul>
<li><strong>Materials</strong> ‚Äì Creating realistic objects require a look a feel with what we do interact with in our day to day lives. Materials are data that is assigned to the surface/faces of objects to make it appear a certain way when rendered. They include but not limited to iron, steel, leather, wool, etc.  </li>
</ul></li>
</ul>

<p><br /></p>

<ul>
<li><p><strong><em>Learning the SDK</em></strong> ‚Äì With the UI basics covered, learning the SDK is less overwhelming. So, how do you go about it?</p>

<ul>
<li><strong>Hello World!</strong> ‚Äì As any standard practice, begin with a hello world program. 3ds Max SDK documentation has a good tutorial to hep you do exactly this. Check out <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=lesson_1_sample_utility_plug-in">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=lesson_1_sample_utility_plug-in</a> on how to begin a simple utility plugin. <em>[I do assume you did setup the plugin wizard on your visual studio installation]</em>. The code sample below shows a text Hello World on the prompt stack in the 3ds Max UI. <br />
<br />
<code>
ip-&gt;PushPrompt(_M("Hello World from Lesson 1"));
</code> <br />
<br /></li>
</ul>

<p>With that out of the way and well understood, lets now look at other concepts of the SDK.  </p>

<ul>
<li>3ds Max SDK: The Learning Path ‚Äì This is a series of lessons covering different aspects of the SDK. The tutorial is available at <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=3ds_max_sdk_-_the_learning_path">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=3ds_max_sdk_-<em>the</em>learning_path</a>. Let‚Äôs have a rundown of what it entails:</li>
<li><strong><em>Sample Utility</em></strong> ‚Äì This is the hello world program for a utility plugin. Will give you a rundown of what it takes to setup a plugin project, explanation of all files in the project as well as what the different functions generated by the plug-in wizard generated.</li>
<li><strong><em>Scene Graphs &amp; Nodes</em></strong> ‚Äì Scene objects (geometric objects, lights, cameras, etc.) in 3ds Max and the relationship with each other are stored in a scene graph. This gives a good understanding of the scene graph structure, how to transverse the scene graph and manipulate the nodes (add, remove, update as well as a sample code that shows a simple graph exporter into a text file.</li>
<li><strong><em>Reference System</em></strong> ‚Äì Think of this to get updates from changes when entity changes in scene. From a Qt background, think of it has the signal/slot mechanism but way different. This gives an understanding of how plugins can propagate changes on scene through which other plugins/objects can get the changes. A good understanding of this subject will make it easy developing plugins since most times plugins depend on external data on scene and need to be notified of the changes as well as modify them and cause appropriate change propagation.</li>
<li><strong><em>Animation Controllers</em></strong> ‚Äì These are plugins that provide 3ds Max the value of a parameter for a scene object at any given time. Think of it as a function that given the time (keyframe timestamp) it returns the property value at the given time. This section goes through how to implement a simple controller to achieve scene object animation over time.</li>
<li><strong><em>Geometric Objects</em></strong> ‚Äì On the 3ds Max scene, objects created by mouse clicks, or any other means is because of combination of one or more geometric shapes. This is used for creating 2D shapes like circles, squares, boxes, triangles, etc. or even 3d like cylinder, box, etc. God understanding of this gives enough knowledge to aid in developing custom shapes and objects on scene or even modify existing shapes. </li>
<li><strong><em>Parameter Blocks</em></strong> ‚Äì This is a 3ds Max way of reading from and writing to plug-in parameter values which is independent of the plug-in type. This is 3ds Max specific implementation giving ease of sharing plugin data, easy updates by other plugins, easy serialization, etc. This section seems intimidating at first to grasp but it‚Äôs one of the most critical to understand well for you to develop plugins that can maintain and share parameter states with other plugins. <br />
<br />
<br /></li>
</ul></li>
<li><p><strong>3ds Max Webcast Tutorials</strong> ‚Äì Similar to the learning path above, the webcast was initially done as virtual tutorials to train on 3ds max SDK topics with assignments after each topic. Unlike the learning path, the webcast goes an in-depth with explanations of why thigs are done the way they are done. This gives a better understanding of the concepts conveyed both in the documentations and the learning path tutorials. With an addition of assignments after each section, this gives room to try out from knowledge learnt with assurance of explanation of the required response if not well understood or if stuck. Although this content is old, upgrade of such content is underway. Let‚Äôs look at the main sections that prove to be useful for a beginner.</p>

<ul>
<li><strong><em>General 3ds Max customization Introduction</em></strong> ‚Äì This goes through 3ds Max UI overview and how it can be customized, a rundown of MAXScript usage in scene objects manipulation, the .NET API in 3ds Max and 3ds Max SDK usage.</li>
<li>Getting started in the 3ds Max SDK basics ‚Äì This section goes into the SDK basics, terminologies, plug-in types, and a rundown of the basic scene concepts (Scene, Node, References, Parameter Blocks, Animation, etc.)</li>
<li><strong><em>Transformation and Scene, Node, Scene Graph</em></strong> ‚Äì Scene objects are represented by Nodes on the scene graph. So, this section explains how transformation (translation, rotation, scale) of the scene is done, scene compositions, scene objects and scene graphs manipulation &amp; its traversing.</li>
<li><strong><em>Reference System</em></strong> ‚Äì If you didn‚Äôt understand how reference systems work from the Learning path, this will be your teacher. It goes in-depth on how reference systems work, the logic behind, as well as good/bad practices in reference systems in 3ds Max.</li>
<li><strong><em>Parameter Blocks and Function Publishing</em></strong> ‚Äì Similar to what is detailed in the learning path, this explains parameter blocks systems, its implementation and expound on the concepts that make it such a powerful concept behind the 3ds Max robustness. In addition, this section goes to give an introduction into function publishing - a concept for exposing functions in C++ to the MAXScript.</li>
<li><strong><em>Geometry Fundamentals</em></strong> ‚Äì Further from what was covered by the geometry section of the learning paths, this section goes further into covering shapes, splines, patches, and meshes in the making &amp; manipulation of scene objects.</li>
<li><strong><em>Modifiers</em></strong> ‚Äì Similar to what was mentioned under 3s Max UI learning, modifiers here look at how to make custom modifiers that manipulate objects, edits, mapping coordinates and world space. Such modifiers are bend, taper, twist, extrude, surface, etc.   </li>
</ul></li>
</ul>

<p><br /></p>

<h1>Tips &amp; Tricks</h1>

<p>Fast learning does exist, but pitfalls are the hindering factor. Here are my suggestions based on what I did learn in my journey:  </p>

<p><br /></p>

<ul>
<li><em>Use the Webcast &amp; the Learning path tandem</em> ‚Äì Some of us like reading, some like watching, depending who you are, try watching the concepts and listening to the in-depth explanations then later go do the reading on the learning path and/or the 3ds Max SDK documentation. This may save you hours of wondering what you are reading.</li>
<li><em>Don‚Äôt go too deep</em> ‚Äì Quite controversial, but, if your intent is to work with the SDK then, take care you don‚Äôt get too deep learning the UI. Autodesk gives recommendation of tutorials to follow to learn the UI section, which is very detailed. You may look at specific sections to know the basics then later go deeper as needed.</li>
<li><em>C++ is important!</em> ‚Äì Learning the SDK requires some level of understanding C++ concepts. Sharpen your knowledge/skills there first since there is less/no explanations of such concepts once you start working with the SDK.</li>
<li><em>Be careful with burnout</em> ‚Äì Yes, this is real. The SDK concepts are a lot, I don‚Äôt expect you to master all in a single day. Give yourself time, rest whenever you feel overwhelmed, and most important ‚Äì reach out for any questions.</li>
<li><em>Make SDK examples &amp; samples your charm!</em> ‚Äì The 3ds Max SDK ships with samples and example code which you can refer to see how things were implemented. Be careful to always change the plug-in class IDs to avoid conflicts with the default implemented plug-ins. </li>
<li><em>Check attached samples for tutorials</em> ‚Äì Both the Learning path and webcast material have completed code samples. Check on them in case things are not working as expected. The Learning path and the webcast Github/videos/materials can be found in the links below.</li>
</ul>

<hr />

<p>Learning Path Github Repository - <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Learning-Path">https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Learning-Path</a> <br />
3ds Max Developer Center - <a href="https://www.autodesk.com/developer-network/platform-technologies/3ds-max#3dsmax-sdk">https://www.autodesk.com/developer-network/platform-technologies/3ds-max#3dsmax-sdk</a>  </p>

<p><br />  </p>

<blockquote>
  <p>Developer center provides 3ds Max SDK Training Webcasts in both <a href="http://download.autodesk.com/media/adn/3dsMax_July2012_Webcast_final_Recording.zip">English</a> and <a href="https://images.autodesk.com/adsk/files/3dsMax_SDK_webcast_Japanese.zip">Japanese</a> and a separate <a href="http://download.autodesk.com/media/adn/3dsMax_July2012_Webcast_final_TrainingMaterial.zip">Download</a> for the training materials. Videos are provided in a zip file.  </p>
</blockquote>

<hr />

<p><br /></p>

<p><strong><em>I hope this will help you in your journey to learning 3ds Max SDK.</em></strong>   </p>

<p><br /></p>

<p>Any question? Any suggestion? Feel free to reach out!</p>

<div>
<h1 id="building-a-custom-value-type-for-maxscript">Building a custom value type for MAXScript</h1>
</div>
<div>
<p><strong>3ds MAX</strong> is a is a professional 3D computer graphics program that can be used to create 3D animations, models, games, and images. The power that it can do comes not only from the robust UI (User Interface) tools and ease of building plugins but also from the inbuilt scripting capability using Autodesk MAXScript. It is no doubt the power that MAXScript adds to 3ds Max. It is a great scripting method for automation, animation, object creation and manipulation. Lately, it has become the core of initiating 3ds Max Design Automation in the Autodesk Platform Services (formerly Forge).</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2 id="object-manipulation-using-maxscript">Object Manipulation using MAXScript</h2>
</div>
<div>
<p>To manipulate objects in scene (create, modify, animate, etc.), the returned object on the Maxscript side must give you access to the underlying exposed properties. Let us create a simple box object and look at the exposed properties that the object has.</p>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Open 3ds MAX software and launch the Maxscript listener window (sample shown in the image below). To launch the listener window, check the steps outlined here <a href="https://knowledge.autodesk.com/support/3ds-max/learn-explore/caas/CloudHelp/cloudhelp/2015/ENU/3DSMax/files/GUID-C8019A8A-207F-48A0-985E-18D47FAD8F36-htm.html">https://knowledge.autodesk.com/support/3ds-max/learn-explore/caas/CloudHelp/cloudhelp/2015/ENU/3DSMax/files/GUID-C8019A8A-207F-48A0-985E-18D47FAD8F36-htm.html</a>.<br /><br /></p>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_2.png" /></p>
</li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Let us create and add a box object to the scene. Add the command <code>box1 = box()</code>.</p>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_3.png" /></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The command above creates a primitive type of box object with the name Box001 at x,y,z (0,0,0) as shown below.</p>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_4.png" /></p>
</li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Let us begin by viewing all the exposed properties of the box object. We use the command <code>getPropNames &lt;object_name&gt;</code> i.e., <code>getPropNames box1</code>. This returns a thorough list of properties <strong># (<em>#typeinCreationMethod, #typeInPos, #typeInLength, #typeInWidth, #typeInHeight, #length, #width, #height, #widthsegs, #lengthsegs, #heightsegs, #mapcoords, #realWorldMapSize</em>)</strong></p>
</li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>We can therefore manipulate the created scene object by changing the values of the associated properties.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-python">  box1<span class="hljs-selector-class">.length</span> = <span class="hljs-number">45</span>
  box1<span class="hljs-selector-class">.width</span> = <span class="hljs-number">100</span>
  box1<span class="hljs-selector-class">.height</span> = <span class="hljs-number">300</span>
</code></pre>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_5.png" /></p>
</li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Resultant object on scene is as shown below (notice changes in size as compared to the initial box object)</p>
<img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_6.png" /></li>
</ul>
</div>
<div>
<blockquote>
<p>As noted, each object type on the 3ds MAX does pose some properties that can be manipulated from the MAXScript side. A similar approach can be used to view properties for other objects like <strong>Sphere</strong>, <strong>Cylinder</strong>, <strong>Cone</strong>, etc.</p>
</blockquote>
</div>
<div>
<p>&#0160;</p>
</div>
<div>
<h1 id="making-custom-properties">Making Custom Properties</h1>
</div>
<div>
<p>Building your own custom objects may require you to set up your own custom properties exposed to the MAXScript. This is important as many a times we use primitive objects to build complex objects that we may need to access and manipulate from the MAXScript. As such, any data exposed to MAXScript from the C++ side inherits from the Value type. You can read more about how Value type work in MAXScript here <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=GUID-911865D9-A5F9-4686-B01A-243308F41C55">https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=GUID-911865D9-A5F9-4686-B01A-243308F41C55</a>.</p>
</div>
<div>
<h2 id="creating-a-custom-value-type">Creating a Custom Value Type</h2>
</div>
<div>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In your project, add a new class to your project, let us call it <code>CustomValue</code>, inheriting the <code>Value</code> type as shown below.</p>
<img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_7.png" /></li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>With that set, add the following snippets to your <code>.h</code> file</p>
<pre><code>
        #include &lt;maxscript/maxscript.h&gt;
        #include &lt;maxscript/foundation/numbers.h&gt;
        #include &lt;maxscript/foundation/3dmath.h&gt;
    
        #include &quot;resource.h&quot;

        #ifdef ScripterExport
        #undef ScripterExport
        #endif
        #define ScripterExport __declspec( dllexport )

        <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> CustomValue : <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> Value
        {
        <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span>:
            ENABLE_STACK_ALLOCATE(CustomValue);

            <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span>        <span class="hljs-title">collect</span><span class="hljs-params">()</span> </span>{ <span class="hljs-keyword">delete</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>; }
            <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span>        <span class="hljs-title">sprin1</span><span class="hljs-params">(CharStream* s)</span></span>;
            <span class="hljs-function">Value* <span class="hljs-title">get_property</span><span class="hljs-params">(Value** arg_list, <span class="hljs-keyword">int</span> count)</span></span>;
            <span class="hljs-function">Value* <span class="hljs-title">set_property</span><span class="hljs-params">(Value** arg_list, <span class="hljs-keyword">int</span> count)</span></span>;

            <span class="hljs-comment">// Generic commands for copying/deleting/showing properties/etc.</span>
            def_generic(<span class="hljs-keyword">delete</span>, <span class="hljs-string">&quot;delete&quot;</span>);
            def_generic(copy, <span class="hljs-string">&quot;copy&quot;</span>);
            def_generic(show_props, <span class="hljs-string">&quot;showProperties&quot;</span>);
            def_generic(get_props, <span class="hljs-string">&quot;getPropNames&quot;</span>);
        };

        
        </code></pre>
<ul>
<li>What do these functions do?
<ul>
<li><code>void sprin1(CharStream* s)</code> ‚Äì returns a string representation of the object. When instantiating the object from MAXScript, a string is returned showing the default or set values.</li>
<li><code>Value* get_property(Value** arg_list, int count)</code> ‚Äì Used to get property values into the MAXScript side. When a property is accessed from the MAXScript i.e., during computation, this function is called automatically, and it returns the current set value of the property.</li>
<li><code>Value* set_property(Value** arg_list, int count)</code> ‚Äì Similar to get_property, but in this case use to pass a new value from the MAXScript to the c++. Basically, used to update property values. It is also called automatically when assigning a value to a property. I.e., <em>box1.pos = [0.5,3.4,5.6]</em></li>
<li><code>def_generic(get_props, &quot;getPropNames&quot;)</code> ‚Äì Defines a generic property called <code>getPropNames</code> used in Maxscript to return all property names that can be accessed from MAXScript and maps it to an internal function in our class called <code>get_props</code>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>With all declarations done, let&#39;s now implement the functionality before adding new property types to our class.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-c++">    <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::get_property(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
    {
        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>::get_property(arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>);
    }

    <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::set_property(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
    {
        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>::set_property(arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>);
    }

    <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::delete_vf(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
    {
        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> &amp;ok;
    }


    <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::copy_vf(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
    {
        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> this;
    }

    void
    CustomValue::sprin1(CharStream* s)
    {
        // String reprentation of the <span class="hljs-keyword">data</span> ie Point3Vales
    }

    <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::get_props_vf(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
    {
        // getPropNames &lt;max_object&gt; [#dynamicOnly] -- returns array of prop names of wrapped obj

        MAXScript_TLS* _tls = (MAXScript_TLS*)TlsGetValue(thread_locals_index);
        one_typed_value_local_tls(Array * result);
        vl.result = new Array(<span class="hljs-number">0</span>);
        return_value_tls(vl.result);
    }

    <span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::show_props_vf(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
    {
        // showProperties &lt;max_object&gt; [_T(<span class="hljs-string">&quot;prop_pat&quot;</span>)] [to:&lt;<span class="hljs-keyword">file</span>&gt;]   - applies to ref0 <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> the wrapper

        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> &amp;false_value;
    }
</code></pre>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Let us add new properties. First, a property is defined as follows.</p>
<ul>
<li><code>def_property(&lt;property name&gt;)</code> ‚Äì Added to the class</li>
<li><code>Value* CustomValue::get_&lt;property name&gt;(Value** arg_list, int count)</code> ‚Äì getter function for the property</li>
<li><code>Value* CustomValue::set_&lt;property name&gt;(Value** arg_list, int count)</code> ‚Äì setter function for the property</li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Let us create a couple of properties that can be manipulated from Max side. We define it as follows.</p>
<ul>
<li><code>Point3 m_pos</code> ‚Äì A Point3 object that we intend to expose to MAXScript</li>
<li><code>def_property(pos)</code> ‚Äì A property called pos that we will return the m_pos above</li>
<li><code>def_property(x)</code> ‚Äì The x-coordinate of the Point3 m_pos created</li>
<li><code>def_property(y)</code> ‚Äì The y-coordinate of the Point3 m_pos created</li>
<li><code>def_property(z)</code> ‚Äì The z-coordinate of the Point3 m_pos created</li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Consequently, lets create the setter and getter functions for each of the properties above i.e.,</p>
<pre><code class="lang-c++"><span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::get_pos(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
{
    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> new Point3Value(m_pos);
}

<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>* CustomValue::set_pos(<span class="hljs-keyword">Value</span>** arg_list, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">count</span>)
{
    m_pos = arg_list[<span class="hljs-number">0</span>]-&gt;to_point3();
    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> arg_list[<span class="hljs-number">0</span>];
}
</code></pre>
<p>For the <strong><em>x,y,z</em></strong> properties, it is like the implementation above. Check the full code link attached for the implementation. Implement the <code>get_props_vf</code> function by adding the four properties to the result array.</p>
<h3 id="last-touches-">Last touches:</h3>
<ul>
<li>Added the 4 properties to the <code>get_props_vf()</code> function in the result array</li>
<li>Add a default constructor for the CustomValue and instantiate the <em>m_pos</em> variable to a Point3 value</li>
<li>Bonus, implement the <code>show_props_vf()</code> function in the <code>CustomValue.cpp</code></li>
</ul>
<p><br /><br /><br /></p>
<h1 id="bonus-tip-">Bonus Tip!</h1>
<h3 id="building-and-running-the-snippet-above">Building and Running the Snippet above</h3>
<hr />
<blockquote>
<p>This assumes you have already installed Visual Studio, 3ds MAX and 3ds MAX SDK. Check on how to setup the 3ds Max SDK and plugin wizard if you do not have that already. This is covered in the 3ds MAX documentation here <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=installing_the_plug-in_wizard_ap">http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=installing_the_plug-in_wizard_ap</a></p>
</blockquote>
<hr />
<p><br />To enable us to build and run our created class, we will be using a StaticInteface in a Global Utility interface (GUT) plugin type in 3ds MAX SDK. Let us first create a global utility object (GUT) using the Plugin Wizard. The wizard will create a barebone project with all required functions for us to implement them.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_8.png" /></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Next, we will add a static interface to expose a static object to the 3ds MAX side. This is the instance we will be using when getting and manipulating properties from the MAXScript. In Visual Studio, add a new class, let us call it ADNStaticInterface and add the following snippets.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-c++"><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> ADNStaticInterface : <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> FPStaticInterface 
{

<span class="hljs-keyword">public</span>:

    <span class="hljs-comment">// The follow exposes our functions to Max</span>
    <span class="hljs-keyword">enum</span> FN_IDS {
        fn_run1
    };
    <span class="hljs-function">BEGIN_FUNCTION_MAP                
        <span class="hljs-title">FN_0</span><span class="hljs-params">(fn_run1, TYPE_VALUE, run1)</span></span>;
    END_FUNCTION_MAP

    <span class="hljs-comment">// Implement the functions exposed above</span>
    <span class="hljs-function">Value* <span class="hljs-title">run1</span><span class="hljs-params">()</span></span>;

    <span class="hljs-comment">// General purpose exposure</span>
    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> ADNStaticInterface* <span class="hljs-title">GetInstance</span><span class="hljs-params">()</span> </span>{ <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> &amp;_theInstance; }

<span class="hljs-keyword">private</span>:
    DECLARE_DESCRIPTOR(ADNStaticInterface);

    <span class="hljs-comment">// The single instance of this class</span>
    <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> ADNStaticInterface _theInstance;

    <span class="hljs-comment">// Point3CustomValue *m_customValue;</span>
    CustomValue* m_customValue;
};
</code></pre>
<p>We first begin by exposing our function to MAX; first an Enum of function ids <code>(fn_run1)</code></p>
<ul>
<li><code>Value* run1()</code> - This defines a function that will be called from Maxscript and returns a Value type. The return value object will allow manipulation of the properties.</li>
<li><code>static ADNStaticInterface* GetInstance()</code> ‚Äì Returns a static access object</li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Let us implement the declared functions. Beginning with the</p>
<pre><code class="lang-c++">
ADNStaticInterface ADNStaticInterface::_theInstance
(
    IADN_STATIC_INTERFACE, _T(<span class="hljs-string">&quot;ADN&quot;</span>), 0, NULL, FP_CORE,
    ADNStaticInterface::fn_run1, _T(<span class="hljs-string">&quot;run1&quot;</span>), 0, TYPE_VALUE, 0, 0,

    p_end
);
</code></pre>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The function declares an ADN (Autodesk Developer Network) object that can be used from the MAX side to call the functions in the C++ side.</p>
<pre><code class="lang-c++">Value* ADNStaticInterface::run1()
{
    Point3Value* nValue = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> Point3Value(<span class="hljs-number">0.0</span>, <span class="hljs-number">0.0</span>, <span class="hljs-number">0.0</span>);

    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> nValue;
}
</code></pre>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The run1 function returns an object to the MAXScript side. We have just set up a Point3Value to be returned to the MAXScript. The Point3Value is a Point3 type which inherits from the Value class to enable exposing the values to MAXScript.</p>
<p>Let us build and run the code to test if all works so far. Run the project within visual studio, with 3ds MAX launched, open the MAXScript listener window and run the command <code>apt = adn.run1()</code>, you should be getting an output like below.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_9.png" /></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>If that works so far, let us now proceed to building our own custom value type. Remember all values exposed to Maxscript must be of the Value type (inherits from the value type).</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Running the custom value to the Static Interface Attach the new CustomValue to the <code>ADNStaticInterface</code> class and return it in the <code>run1()</code> method.</p>
<ul>
<li>Include the custom value header to the <code>ADNStaticInterface.h</code></li>
<li>Add a private member object of the <code>CustomValue</code> type i.e., <code>CustomValue* m_value</code></li>
<li>In the <code>run1()</code> function, instantiate the CustomValue and return it from the function.</li>
</ul>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Run the program and manipulate the properties as shown below.</p>
<p><img alt="3ds Max Design Window" src="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/allankkoech/mne-blogs/master/img/20230120_10.png" /></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Check out the full project code attached or from the git link below. </p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><a href="https://github.com/allankkoech/maxscript-custom-value-type-3dsmax/tree/master">Source Code on Github</a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><br /><br /></p>
<hr />
<p>I hope that was quite descriptive way of creating your own custom value type for MAXScript. I would love to hear if you find better ways of doing it.</p>
<p>Any questions? Feel free to reach out. Cheers!</p>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

BODY:
<p>Hopefully by now you have seen the new release of 3ds Max. For a overview of the new features, check out the help <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2023/ENU/?guid=GUID-F5D297BB-5141-4395-9FFE-3CAD86204D64">here.</a> The Autodesk AREA site has also bee revamped, to be more community oriented. This makes exchanging materials between 3ds Max and Maya easier, but also extends to other tools, including the Forge Viewer.</p>

Highlights include Instance Display API, Instance Rendering API, and Volume Display API. Another aspect improved is the <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2023/ENU/?guid=packaging_plugins">Plugin Packages.</a></p>

AUTHOR: Kevin Vandecar

TITLE: Tips for troubleshooting Visual Studio output and getting Qt to work with 3ds Max SDK
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: tips-for-troubleshooting-visual-studio-output-and-getting-qt-to-work-with-3ds-max-sdk
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: qt
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2021/05/tips-for-troubleshooting-visual-studio-output-and-getting-qt-to-work-with-3ds-max-sdk.html 
DATE: 05/21/2021 03:56:57 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Let&#39;s start with the background leading up to this article... I had a question where I needed to build a Qt sample, specifically this one: <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">&lt;install&gt;\maxsdk\howto\qtObjectDemo.</span> I wanted to continue setting up my newer laptop and had not installed Qt yet, and was just getting 3ds Max 2022 setup. I am using Visual Studio 2019, but of course targeting the MSVC 2017 toolset (141).</p>
<p>First, the output window in Visual Studio does not always tell you the details of what went wrong with a build action. I learned recently the amount of detail can be configured through the ‚ÄúBuild and Run‚Äù settings. By default it seems the setting is ‚ÄúMinimal‚Äù. You can find the setting in ‚ÄúOptions‚Äù, which can be found in at least two places: the Debug menu and also Tools menu. For example, navigate to the ‚ÄúTools‚Äù-&gt;‚ÄùOptions‚Äù and then select ‚ÄúProjects and Solutions‚Äù in the left list of categories. Under that category, select ‚ÄúBuild and Run‚Äù and then you will see two drop downs titled ‚ÄúMSBuild project build <strong>output</strong> verbosity‚Äù and ‚ÄúMSBuild project build <strong>log</strong> verbosity‚Äù. In my setup, these are set to <strong>Minimal</strong> at start.</p>
<p>Why would you need to change this? Anytime the output window shows you an error, but does not give enough information! In my case, again, I was trying to compile the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">&lt;install&gt;\maxsdk\howto\qtObjectDemo</span> sample. To build an individual sample, I usually just open the vcxproj into a text editor and change the &#0160;&lt;MaxSDK&gt; entry to the Windows environment variable that is created when installing the SDK. For example in 2022, my entry looks like this: <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">ADSK_3DSMAX_SDK_2022=D:\me\3dsmax\maxsdk2022\maxsdk</span>, so dropping $(ADSK_3DSMAX_SDK_2022) into that MaxSDK definition is enough for the Max SDK components to be found (include, libraries, tools).<br /><br />The issue came -up with a failed build and when the ‚Äúminimal‚Äù output said: ‚ÄúThe system cannot find the path specified.‚Äù Very helpful‚Ä¶ Not. Ok, I‚Äôll get to the troubleshooting help after we talk about Qt.</p>
<p>The next topic to include here is the Qt tools. Let‚Äôs start by reminding you about Qt. 3ds Max started to include Qt in the 3ds Max 2017 release. Each release requires a different version of Qt to correspond to the 3ds Max version used for each major release. You will find the specifics in the SDK Requirements docs. For 2022 see <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_about_the_3ds_max_sdk_sdk_requirements_html">here</a>. The good news is that only the 3ds Max 2017 release required a ‚Äúpatched‚Äù version of Qt (available in pre-built form on the <a href="https://www.autodesk.com/develop3dsmax">3ds Max developer center</a>. All versions after that are using the default source and binaries from Qt directly.</p>
<p>Next comes installing Qt‚Ä¶ Qt distributions are a bit interesting. They now have a commercial version, and an open source version. As a developer, you will need to decide which version is appropriate for your business. Either version will install Visual Studio specific versions. So, if you are supporting multiple 3ds Max versions, you will also need to install multiple versions of Qt, and their Qt Maintenance Tool can help you to stay updated as you move forward. For example, I installed these for my new machine:<br /><br /><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0278802b03f8200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Qt_versions" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0278802b03f8200d image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0278802b03f8200d-800wi" title="Qt_versions" /></a><br />Again, for me, I needed to setup a new machine, and also at same time was setting up for the recent 3ds Max 2022 release, I was able to select the versions listed from the 3ds Max SDK Requirements‚Ä¶ After the Qt installation (which took some time), it also helps to have the Visual Studio Qt Extension. From the SDK docs, see step 2 <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_writing_plug_ins_using_qt_with_3ds_max_plug_ins_html">here</a>.</p>
<p>In my case, I was setting up Visual Studio 2019 Professional IDE (to use with the msvc2017 toolset (141)). The place to install the Qt Extension is on a menu called ‚ÄúExtensions‚Äù. Here you can click ‚ÄúManage‚Äù and search for Qt and then install it.<br /><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0282e10368e7200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Qt_tools" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0282e10368e7200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0282e10368e7200b-800wi" title="Qt_tools" /></a><br /><br />Next, using the Qt Extension, you can configure Visual Studio to use the versions you installed‚Ä¶ Note you can find it in the MSVS Options area after it is installed‚Ä¶ Or direct from the Extensions menu:<br /><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0282e10368ed200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Qt_config" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0282e10368ed200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0282e10368ed200b-800wi" title="Qt_config" /></a></p>
<p>You‚Äôll click &lt;add new Qt version&gt; to configure and add your installed versions and locations.</p>
<p>Ok, now going back to the 3ds Max project, and trying to build‚Ä¶&#0160; In the options for ‚ÄúBuild and Run‚Äù you will see two drop downs titled ‚ÄúMSBuild project build <strong>output</strong> verbosity‚Äù and for me was set to ‚ÄúMinimal‚Äù where I got this output:<br /><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0282e10368fb200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Vs_min_output" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0282e10368fb200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0282e10368fb200b-800wi" title="Vs_min_output" /></a></p>
<p>Note the two Qt commands at beginning‚Ä¶ Those are output from the 3ds Max Project file. They are one after another, then the error occurs 2x times. At first I did not think of Qt being an issue, but after we change the MSVS output option to be ‚ÄúDetailed‚Äù we get a lot more information in the output window. It takes a close eye, but I was suspecting Qt now (because other non-Qt projects were building fine). So, in the output Window I did a search for Qt (Ctrl-F), and bam‚Ä¶ right away I see some suspicious issues for example:<br /><br /><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">1&gt;Property reassignment: $(QtMigrateLib)=&quot;D:\me\3dsmax\maxsdk2022\maxsdk\QtWinMigrate\lib\&quot; (previous value: &quot;D:\me\QtWinMigrate\lib\&quot;) at D:\me\3dsmax\maxsdk2022\maxsdk\ProjectSettings\PropertySheets\3dsmax.general.project.settings.props (237,3)</span></p>
<p>Notice it is coming from the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">maxsdk\ProjectSettings\PropertySheets\3dsmax.general.project.settings.props</span> file‚Ä¶</p>
<p>Later (towards end where the actual build errors are) I also see the calls to Qt uic.exe and moc.exe tools for this project. For example:<br /><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">1&gt;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160; &quot;D:\me\3dsmax\maxsdk2022\maxsdk\Qt\5.15.1\\bin\uic.exe&quot; -o &quot;.\GeneratedFiles\ui_QtPluginRollup.h&quot; &quot;D:\work\sfdc\case17823411\qtObjectDemo\QtPluginRollup.ui&quot;</span></p>
<p>Here‚Äôs where the problem is‚Ä¶ Notice that the front part of the path is 3ds Max SDK, but second part is the versioned Qt path (but missing a Qt platform). This is not the correct way to find Qt. I found that in the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">3dsmax.general.project.settings.props</span> file that 3ds Max team is setting Qt values to be relative to the 3ds Max SDK path. For example: <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">&lt;QTDIR Condition=&quot;&#39;$(IsDefaultQtVsProjectFormat)&#39; == &#39;false&#39;&quot;&gt;$([MSBuild]::ValueOrDefault(`$(QTDIR)`, `$(MaxSdkDir)Qt\$(QTVER)\`))&lt;/QTDIR&gt;</span></p>
<p>That evaluates to something like this: <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">D:\me\3dsmax\maxsdk2022\maxsdk\Qt\5.15.1\\bin\uic.exe<span style="font-family: georgia, palatino;"> and is wrong.</span></span></p>
<p>There are two problems here‚Ä¶ There is the 3ds Max SDK path, and even if we installed there, it could be an issue because there is no Qt ‚Äúplatform‚Äù folder in that evaluation. <br /><br />What is the solution? Well, I found that the easiest was just to set the QTDIR from my VS environment (ie. a VS2019 command prompt). You could also change the QTDIR value in the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">3dsmax.general.project.settings.props</span> file, but that means changing source SDK files, which I always try to avoid (being in support, I want what is shipped, and could also be issues if trying to setup a new environment, how do you remember to change that again?) The local environment variable does not require changes to the 3ds Max SDK props file. <br /><br />For example in a VS2019 command prompt, I was able to: <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">set QTDIR=D:\cc\qt\5.15.1\msvc2019_64 </span>and this overrides the props setting when loading the project from that environment.</p>
<p>I&#39;d be interested to here your feedback or if you found a better way, so feel free to leave a comment.</p>
-----
EXTENDED BODY:

AUTHOR: Kevin Vandecar
AUTHOR EMAIL: kevin.vandecar@autodesk.com
TITLE: Porting a C++ Plugin to 3ds Max 2022 and Installing the 3ds Max 2022 C++ Wizard
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: porting-a-c-plugin-to-3ds-max-2022-and-installing-the-3ds-max-2022-c-wizard
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2021/05/porting-a-c-plugin-to-3ds-max-2022-and-installing-the-3ds-max-2022-c-wizard.html 
DATE: 05/07/2021 02:37:52 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Even though the build tools (toolset) did not change, there were a number of changes made to the 3ds Max SDK that requires a plugin to be ported and recompiled. Because the SDK changed and has new requirements, this affects the binary compatibility.</p>
<p>The first one you are likely to hit, is that all plugins typically have an implementation of the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">ClassDesc2</span> (or <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">ClassDesc</span>, if not needing <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">ParamBlock2</span> support). Minimally you will have to add a new method required by the underlying base <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">ClassDesc</span>, <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">NonLocalizedClassName</span>. Please take a moment to read the article about this aspect <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_localization_html%20">here</a>, especially if you are providing localized plugins.</p>
<p>I also noticed that the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">Matrix3</span> class has changed. Depending on how you are using it, and your warning/error level you use in your projects, you may have to update code (or the project). The changes are documented <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_modeling_html#changes-to-class-matrix3-and-dmatrix3-">here</a>. In the case of the ADN Bake Radiosity example, the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">Matrix3</span> was initialed using the old constructor (which takes a BOOL and remember BOOL in 3ds Max is an int type). You will still see this syntax scattered throughout the SDK samples, and rather than fixing their code, they are using the ‚Äù<span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">MAX_SILENCE_DEPRECATED_MATRIX_BOOL_CTOR</span> ‚Äú definition to silence the warning. In my opinion, &#0160;this is a good opportunity to cleanup your own code, though, and you will be in good shape if the SDK team decides to completely remove the deprecated constructor.</p>
<p>Finally, I would like to discuss Visual Studio 2019. Although 3ds Max and other Autodesk products have not moved to VS2019 (and toolset 142), you can use the IDE and be compatible with VS2017 (and toolset 141). This has been the case for a number of VS releases where you can target previous toolsets. With VS 2019, most editions also provide the VS2017 (toolset 141). There is a discussion about it <a href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/cppblog/cpp-binary-compatibility-and-pain-free-upgrades-to-visual-studio-2019/">here</a>. Although they talk about binary compatibility, we advise to stick with the same toolset that 3ds Max is built with to avoid any unknowns. There is nothing worse than tracking down some weird binary incompatibility, and now that VS 2017 (toolset 141) is included with VS2019 there is no reason you cannot use latest greatest IDE and features, while sticking to the official toolset.</p>
<p>One note about VS 2019 and ‚Äúclassic‚Äù wizards like 3ds Max, there is no longer default folder structure that supports an ‚Äúout-of-the-box‚Äù installation. However you can easily create the correct structure to install the 3ds Max Wizard. Also note that there was a bug (found by one of our other ADN engineers here) that was fixed, and requires to have the later builds of VS2019. See <a href="https://vsf-prod.westus.cloudapp.azure.com/content/problem/973397/custom-wizard-vsz-and-template-directory-vsdir-are.html">here</a> for the details.</p>
<p>Here are the steps I would suggest to successfully setup the 3ds Max 2022 wizard in Visual Studio 2019:</p>
<ol>
<li>Make sure VS 2019 is updated to at least v16.5.2. You can find this in the Help -&gt; About dialog.</li>
<li>Create this folder structure if it is not present. Depending on other modules you have installed, this could already be present: <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">&lt;install folder&gt;\msvs2019\Common7\IDE\VC\vcprojects</span></li>
<li>Copy the files from the 3ds Max 2022 SDK folder. These are:
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier; font-size: 10pt;">&lt;install folder&gt;\maxsdk\howto\3dsmaxPluginWizard\3dsmaxPluginWizard.ico</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier; font-size: 10pt;">&lt;install folder&gt;\maxsdk\howto\3dsmaxPluginWizard\3dsmaxPluginWizard.vsdir</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier; font-size: 10pt;">&lt;install folder&gt;\maxsdk\howto\3dsmaxPluginWizard\3dsmaxPluginWizard.vsz</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Open the 3dsmaxPluginWizard.vsz file in a text editor
<ul>
<li>Update the wizard engine to 16:&#0160; &#0160; <br /><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier; font-size: 10pt;">Wizard=VsWizard.VsWizardEngine.16.0</span></li>
<li>Add the path. Note it only worked for me to use forward slash (and before backslash was fine). In my case it was like this: <br /><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier; font-size: 10pt;">Param=&quot;ABSOLUTE_PATH = d:/me/3dsmax/maxsdk2022/maxsdk/howto/3dsmaxPluginWizard&quot;</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<p>After these changes, you should see the Wizard in the Visual Studio 2019 projects now. Also note that you can setup several versions of the Wizard as you want. This only requires adding pertinent information. In my case I like to make sure to use the support wizards for each version of 3ds Max. After setting up 3ds Max 2021 and 3ds Max 2022 in the Visual Studio 2019 environment, I can easily create projects for each version, using the Wizard for each specific version. Because the UI of Visual Studio 2019 has changed, it may not be obvious at first. Here‚Äôs how to find the 3ds Max C++ Wizard...</p>
<ol>
<li>After starting Visual Studio 2019, it will look like this:<br /><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c026bded04ba6200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Fig01" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c026bded04ba6200c image-full img-responsive" height="523" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c026bded04ba6200c-800wi" title="Fig01" width="1003" /></a></li>
<li>Click on ‚ÄúCreate a new project‚Äù (as highlighted in above screenshot).</li>
<li>Now you will see a long list of project types, and C++ is found a long way down if you have installed other types of targets. You can switch to C++, and it still will not display because the 3ds Max Wizard is a classic one, and does not provide the keywords.</li>
<li>In the Search box at the top, search for ‚Äú3ds Max‚Äù and now they will be found. See the red box highlight in below screen shot.</li>
<li>Once you create a project, it will then display in the ‚ÄúRecent project templates‚Äù list. See the yellow box in the below screen shot.<br /><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0263e9a303e4200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Fig02" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0263e9a303e4200b image-full img-responsive" height="667" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0263e9a303e4200b-800wi" title="Fig02" width="1001" /></a></li>
</ol>
<p>Although these are minor things, it is worth mentioning that some of the samples (for example the ADN Bake Radiosity) it was the first time I had to actually update the code in many releases, even when toolsets were upgraded!</p>
<p>As such, please take extra time to properly port your plugins, and as always be diligent with testing.</p>

TITLE: 3ds Max 2022 Customization Update
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: 3ds-max-2022-customization-update
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: Announcement
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: MAXScript
CATEGORY: Python
CATEGORY: qt

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2021/04/3ds-max-2022-customization-update.html 
DATE: 04/16/2021 02:10:03 PM
-----
BODY:
<p style="text-align: center;"><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c026bdecbc88b200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Email-header-interior- Image courtesy of Binyan Studio" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c026bdecbc88b200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c026bdecbc88b200c-800wi" title="Email-header-interior- Image courtesy of Binyan Studio" /></a><br /><span style="font-size: 8pt;">Image courtesy of Binyan Studio</span></p>
<p>When looking for an interesting image to spiff up this post, I found the above image and struck me as especially poignant in these covid-19 times. Given that we have not been able to meet in person, it fits well. Never-the-less it&#39;s an awesome image rendered in 3ds Max by one of our awesome customers. :-) I sincerely hope you and yours have been safe during this time, and continue to be diligent to maintain safety.</p>
<p>Now to the gist of this post.... :-)&#0160; On March 24<sup>th</sup> 3ds Max 2022 was released. 3ds Max 2022 is also available on the Forge platform through the <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/en/docs/model-derivative/v2/change_history/changelog/#release-date-2021-03-24">Model Derivative</a> service and on <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/en/docs/design-automation/v3/developers_guide/overview/">Design Automation.</a> If you are an ADN member, the new release should be in your Autodesk account already. Also note that the <a href="https://www.autodesk.com/develop3dsmax">3ds Max Developer Center </a>has been updated with the SDK and a few modules need for certain SDK samples. The SDK is still provided with the distribution as well, but it is not included in the product installation routine. You can find it in the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">&lt;unzipped distribution&gt;\x64\Tools\MAXSDK</span> folder. You can install just by executing the MSI file. Additionally for ADN members we have the debug/hybrid build posted to the ADN member site.</p>
<p>As always, it is helpful to checkout the new features to be sure any customization you already have takes advantage of new features and are compatible. See the list of new features <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2022/ENU/?guid=GUID-E12C6DDA-8AC5-44BC-9022-D3C034CA504E">here</a>. &#0160;There are release notes provided <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2022/ENU/?guid=3dsMax_ReleaseNotes_3dsmax_2022_releasenotes_2022_whats_fixed_html">here.</a><br /><br /></p>
<h2>3ds Max SDK update</h2>
<h3>2022 is an SDK Break</h3>
<ul>
<li>3ds Max 2022 SDK is not backward compatible with the 3ds Max 2021 SDK</li>
<li>Plugins <strong>must</strong> be rebuilt</li>
<li>New SDK features support
<ul>
<li>Modeling, Viewport, and Scripting</li>
<li>Performance</li>
<li>Robustness (for example, applying <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">const</span> correctness to existing APIs)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Requirements:
<ul>
<li>Microsoft Visual Studio 2017, Platform Toolset v141</li>
<li>Windows SDK 10.0.17134.0</li>
<li>.NET 4.8</li>
<li>Qt 5.15.1</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_about_the_3ds_max_sdk_sdk_requirements_html">Details</a></p>
<h3>Plugin Package changes</h3>
<p>The Plugin Package format is now the preferred way to load plugins. This allows you to maintain your plugins and resources outside of the 3d max environment. No changes are needed to any of the 3ds Max config files or environment. The only requirement is location of the plugin package. In 3ds Max 2022 these two details were added:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">SeriesMax</span> attribute is now required</li>
<li><span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">SeriesMin</span> and <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">SeriesMax</span> now support update versions specifically</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_plugin_package_html">Details</a></p>
<h3>MAXScript localization changes affecting the SDK</h3>
<p>A big change to MAXScript environment includes localization features. 3ds Max 2022 eliminates the need for the dictionaries (maxscrpt.lcl files) by allowing plugins to supply both the English and non-English names of their properties. The changes include:</p>
<ul>
<li>New virtual methods that were added</li>
<li>Non-Virtual methods whose signatures have been updated</li>
<li>Virtual methods that were replaced</li>
<li>Trackview and Controller property and sub-anim name support</li>
<li>New reference message added</li>
<li>New parameter definition tag added</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_localization_html">Details</a></p>
<h3>Software Security</h3>
<p>3ds Max has a new Safe Scene Script Execution feature to protect customers from being hacked. For the SDK, a few things have been chaged/added to support this feature:</p>
<ul>
<li>New <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">ISceneScriptSecurityManager</span> interface</li>
<li>SecurityException thrown when an unsafe MAXScript command is blocked</li>
<li>3rd party plugin‚Äôs participation in Safe Scene Script Execution&#0160;</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_security_html">Details</a></p>
<h3>Viewport, Rendering, Materials</h3>
<ul>
<li>New methods to handle the new 3ds Max Presentation Mode feature</li>
<li>Viewport Bloom feature settings are accessible through <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">IViewportViewSettings2</span></li>
<li>Support for customized material creation through the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">IMaterialBrowserEntryInstanceCallback</span> interface. This allows you to register a callback that gets executed when a user creates a material or texture</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_viewport_html">Details</a></p>
<h3>Modeling</h3>
<ul>
<li>Changes to class <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">Matrix3</span> and <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">DMatrix3</span></li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;Now initialized to identity matrix</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;No longer need <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">Matrix3::SetNotIdent()</span></li>
<li>Changes to class <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">TriObjectNormalXTC</span></li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;Performance boost</li>
<li>Changes to class Deformer</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;non-const <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">Map()</span> and <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">IsThreadSafe()</span> are deprecated</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;<span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">MapNormal()</span> has been added and is thread safe</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;<span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">const Map()</span> is now thread safe</li>
<li>New functions added to the <span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">MNMesh</span> class</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;Performance improvement</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;New methods to determine ‚Äúdead‚Äù vertices, edges, and faces via the internal cache</li>
<li>New function added to the Modifier class</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;<span style="font-family: &#39;courier new&#39;, courier;">Modifier::ShouldCollapseOnSave()</span></li>
<li>Improve sub-object picking with High DPI systems</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;Picking with the mouse now properly accounts for high DPI displays</li>
<li>&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;&#0160;You can now better handle High DPI with new methods</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_modeling_html">Details</a></p>
<h3>Miscellaneous Changes and Improvements</h3>
<p>There were also number of miscellaneous changes and improvements.&#0160;</p>
<p><a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Developer_Help_what_s_new_whats_new_3dsmax_2022_sdk_miscellaneous_html">Details</a></p>
<h2>3ds Max .NET API</h2>
<p>There were no API changes to the .NET API environment. However, note that the .NET Framework was updated to 4.8. With Visual Studio, you may need to install this framework before you can update your plugin. You will need to rebuild to ensure it works properly in 3ds Max 2022. Make sure to test functionality as well!</p>
<h2>3ds Max Python</h2>
<p>There were some version updates for the python support. The complete history and summary is <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=Max_Python_API_what_s_new_in_3ds_max_python_api_html">here</a>. These are the versions of various components needed to work with 3ds Max 2022:</p>
<ul>
<li>Python version: 3.7.9</li>
<li>Python PySide: 5.15.1</li>
</ul>
<h3>Python deprecations</h3>
<ul>
<li>Python version 2.7 is no longer available (as announced in 2021 release)</li>
<li>The MaxPlus module is now fully deprecated and no longer available (as announced in 2021 release). Use pymxs module as the python API now.</li>
</ul>
<h3>Python samples</h3>
<p>As introduced in 3ds Max 2021, we have added a github repo for Python samples. Find all the sample here: <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Python-HowTos">https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Python-HowTos</a></p>
<h2>MAXScript</h2>
<p>See the help docs for a complete summary of the changes to MAXScript. Find it <a href="https://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2022/ENU/?guid=What-s-New-in-MAXScript-in-3ds">here</a>.</p>
