TITLE: Announcing 3ds Max 2021! - Customization Update
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: announcing-3ds-max-2021-customization-update
CATEGORY: Announcement
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: Forge
CATEGORY: MAXScript
CATEGORY: Python
CATEGORY: qt

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2020/05/announcing-3ds-max-2021-customization-update.html 
DATE: 05/06/2020 04:21:13 PM
-----
BODY:
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0263e945e80f200b-pi"><img alt="3dsmax2021header" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0263e945e80f200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0263e945e80f200b-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="3dsmax2021header" /></a></p>
<p>Welcome to 3ds Max 2021 API update! On March 27<sup>th</sup>, the new version of 3ds max was released. Shortly after, in early April, the 3ds Max Design Automation engine and Model Derivative Forge services were also updated to 3ds Max 2021. The following is a summary of features and changes in 3ds Max 2021 including customization aspects for customers and developers.&#0160;</p>
<p>If you are interested to know more about Forge Design Automation for 3ds Max, check out this webinar: <a href="https://youtu.be/sWJwo7du8vQ">https://youtu.be/sWJwo7du8vQ</a></p>
<h2>General Feature Summary</h2>
<p>The following is a brief summary of the most important new features in 3ds Max 2021:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-B67A2495-89E4-464A-8913-35C957E950EB"><strong>New Bake to Texture Tool</strong></a> ‚Äì a new tool to bake maps and generate surface maps, supports PBR workflows, Mikk-t normal, and more</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-D7AB420B-F298-4AC5-A3D0-403D75AE1551"><strong>Physically Based Rendering (PBR) Materials</strong></a> ‚Äì physical material is the default throughout 3ds Max, new simplified physical material</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-6BFC22D5-D9DA-45BC-87A7-D95BFAD083E1"><strong>New Weighted Normals Modifier</strong></a> ‚Äì based on popular user request we added support for weighted normals to be calculated and applied to models in 3ds Max</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-CB9141FC-2D52-4EDA-8F78-2351AB53B31B"><strong>New OSL Shaders</strong></a> - Color Correction, HDRI Environment, HDRI Lights, Float&#0160;and&#0160;Color Curves, Camera Projection, Object Projection, Spherical Projection, Uber Noise</li>
<li><strong>Arnold 6 as default renderer </strong>‚Äì Right out of the box, 3ds Max 2021 offers a modern, high-end renderer</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-6D37AD76-09F9-4DA9-90E5-F3286EAD8EF4"><strong>New Substance plugin</strong></a> ‚Äì supports the new ‚ÄúSubstance2‚Äù map, uses latest Substance engine and up to 8k textures</li>
<li><strong>New Install Experience</strong> - the online and offline installation has been overhauled for a simpler and faster experience</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-F7863988-D3A3-47AD-9436-C4EFD023975D"><strong>Scene Converter</strong></a><strong> - </strong>the Scene Converter&#39;s new and improved workflow makes creating custom conversion rules easy. Presets are locked and cannot be saved over, and you are reminded of unsaved changes before closing the Scene Converter.</li>
<li><strong>Viewport Improvements </strong>‚Äì Viewports support Roughness and Ambient Occlusion, clearer viewport customization options can be saved as presets, performance and other quality improvements</li>
<li><strong>ProSound improvements </strong>- Added support for 24bit wav files and unlimited number of audio clips, and bug fixes</li>
<li><strong>Chamfer Improvements for Edit/Editable Poly</strong> ‚Äì The new chamfer technology already available in the Chamfer modifier has been integrated into Edit Poly Modifier and Editable Poly Shape</li>
<li><strong>Sketchup Import improvements</strong> ‚Äì the ATF based Sketchup Importer now support more features previously available in the legacy Sketchup Importer</li>
<li><strong>User Defined Defaults </strong>- Users can now set their own default values that persists through 3ds Max sessions</li>
</ul>
<h2>Developer Feature Summary</h2>
<ul>
<li><strong>New Developer Help</strong> ‚Äì the documentation for the C++ SDK, Python, MAXScript and MCG are available in a new online publication that is separate from the 3ds Max online help. This will help when searching on common 3ds Max topics, but in a developer/customization context! <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/">The direct link is here.</a></li>
<li><strong>Backward compatibility with 3ds Max 2020</strong> - 3ds Max 2021 is compatible with and will load C++ plugins compiled for 3ds Max 2020. For 3ds Max 2020 plugins packaged as an Application Package Format, <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_application_plugin_package_html">the <strong>SeriesMax</strong> tag has to be 2021</a> in order for 3ds Max 2021 to load them.</li>
<li><a href="https://www.autodesk.com/developer-network/platform-technologies/3ds-max#3dsmax-sdk"><strong>3ds Max SDK download</strong></a> ‚Äì the 3ds Max SDK will be available as a free download on the <a href="https://www.autodesk.com/developer-network/platform-technologies/3ds-max#3dsmax-sdk">Autodesk Developer Network</a> website. It will also ship on the 3ds Max 2021 cd-image (&lt;cd-image&gt;\x64\Tools\MAXSDK), but it is not offered as an optional install item through the new 3ds Max 2021 installer.</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_about_the_3ds_max_python_api_html"><strong>New Python 3 Support</strong></a> ‚Äì the Python 3 interpreter integrated into 3ds Max 2021 offers a modern and robust experience for extending and integrating 3ds Max into production pipelines. Python 2.7 is still supported and can be enabled with a command line switch of environment variable. <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_about_the_3ds_max_python_api_html">See this link for details.</a></li>
<li><strong>Python 3 Samples - </strong>The product team also put together a nice github repo of Python How-to samples. These match the MAXScript tutorials content, but using the newest Python 3 environment. <a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Python-HowTos">See here for details.</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_about_the_3ds_max_python_api_html"><strong>pymxs Python API improvements and MaxPlus Python API deprecation</strong></a> ‚Äì Python developers can confidently migrate from MaxPlus to pymxs knowing that they can access the entire set of functionalities 3ds Max has to offer, and interoperate with MAXScript . The MaxPlus Python API is still available with Python 2.7, but you should consider moving to poymxs, so you can get into Python 3.x because the <a href="https://www.python.org/doc/sunset-python-2/">Python organization has deprecated Python 2.x</a>.</li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_application_plugin_package_html"><strong>Application Plugin Package Format Improvements</strong></a> ‚Äì AMG and OSL shaders, and Scene Converter extension scripts are now supported by the Application Plugin Package Format making it easier to migrate your plugin to it</li>
</ul>
<h2>&#0160;</h2>
<h2>What‚Äôs New in the 3ds Max C++ SDK</h2>
<p><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_html">The documented changes are here.</a></p>
<p>Here is a highlight of the most important things to know:</p>
<h3>No SDK Break</h3>
<p>3ds Max 2021 is binary backward compatible with 3ds Max 2020. Plugins compiled for 3ds Max 2020 will load and work in 3ds Max 2021.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> for 3ds Max 2020 plugins packaged as an Application Package Format, the SeriesMax tag has to be 2021 in order for 3ds Max 2021 to load them.</p>
<h3>Compiler</h3>
<p>3ds Max 2021 is compiled with the same compiler as 3ds Max 2020, namely Visual Studio 2017, toolset 14.1. The header files are now compatible with the Visual Studio /permissive- flag which allows plugin developers to turn on standards-conforming compiler behavior.</p>
<h3>Qt version and configuration</h3>
<p>3ds Max 2021 is using Qt 5.12.5. 3<sup>rd</sup> party 3ds Max plugins that use Qt 5.12 are supported.</p>
<h3>3ds Max SDK Download</h3>
<p>The 3ds Max SDK is now available on the 3ds Max Developer Center. It‚Äôs still provided in most distribution media, but you can download anytime from here. <a href="https://www.autodesk.com/develop3dsmax">https://www.autodesk.com/develop3dsmax</a></p>
<h3><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_application_plugin_package_html">Application Plugin Package Format</a></h3>
<p>The plugin package format has been improved to support AMG and OSL shaders, and also supports the scene converter extensions. <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_application_plugin_package_html">See link here.</a></p>
<h3>Change in behavior regarding loading plugins compiled for a compatible release of 3ds Max</h3>
<p>3ds Max 2021 will not automatically load binary plugin dlls whose run-time requirements specify 2020 as SeriesMax, even though 3ds Max 2021 is binary compatible with 3ds Max 2020. Plugin developers will have to re-publish their plugins with the SeriesMax run-time requirement attribute set to 2021, once they verified that their plugins built against the 3ds Max 2020 SDK works properly in 3ds Max 2021.</p>
<h3>Why use the Application Plugin Package Format?</h3>
<p>Packaging and installing plugins using this format has the following advantages for plugin developers and their users:</p>
<ul>
<li>Plugin installers don‚Äôt need to understand where 3ds Max is installed. Instead 3ds Max will discover and load all plugins that are packaged and described in a way that adheres to the Application Package Format</li>
<li>3ds Max installations are not modified by plugin installers, reducing the risk to break it, and making it easier for the users to un-install 3ds Max and 3<sup>rd</sup> party plugins</li>
<li>Plugins can be installed anywhere, if the <em>ADSK_APPLICATION_PLUGINS</em> environment variable contains a path to the installation directory. It is strongly recommended that plugins offer as default installation path <em>%APPDATA%\Autodesk\ApplicationPlugins\ </em>or<em>%PROGRAMDATA%\Autodesk\ApplicationPlugins\</em></li>
</ul>
<p>We strongly suggest to plugin developers to adopt this plugin packaging and installation format, since support for loading plugins described in configuration files will be dropped in the future.</p>
<p>Note that plugin package format has been supported since 3ds Max 2015.</p>
<h3><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html">New C++ APIs</a></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html#new-apis-for-handling-keyboard-shortcut-files" title="">New APIs for handling keyboard shortcut files</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html#new-message-box-api" title="">New message box API</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html#new-normal-mapping-api" title="">New Normal mapping API</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html#mikk-tangent-support-and-tangent-computation-callback" title="">Mikk Tangent support, and tangent computation callback</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html#new-iautobackup-interface" title="">New IAutoBackup interface</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2021_sdk_new_apis_html#new-modifier-name-change-notification" title="">New modifier name change notification</a></li>
</ul>
<h2>&#0160;</h2>
<h2>What‚Äôs New in 3ds Max Python Scripting</h2>
<p>Python based tools for 3ds Max have been gaining popularity over the last few years. To better support the needs of our tech-savvy users, we are updating our Python support, and improving the Python development experience with 3ds Max. <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_in_3ds_max_python_api_html">See here for all the changes.</a></p>
<h3>MaxPlus Python deprecation</h3>
<p>One thing to make note of‚Ä¶ The MaxPlus Python API is not available with Python 3.7, and it will be deprecated in the future alongside Python 2.7. Currently 3ds Max 2021 still supports MaxPlus in the Python 2.7 environment to help give porting time to pymxs.</p>
<h2>&#0160;</h2>
<h2>What‚Äôs New in MAXScript</h2>
<p>MAXSCript has also been improved for 2021 release. <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/MAXDEV/2021/ENU/?guid=GUID-D42EB461-C7DD-410B-89B3-7D477B030D40">See here for complete list of updates.</a></p>
<h3>Highlights:</h3>
<ul>
<li>The new Bake-To-Texture feature has been exposed to Maxscript as a new utility class.</li>
<li>PluginPackageManager interface has six new APIs for getting information about paths searched for the Scene Converter, OSL, and AMG.&#0160; See the ‚ÄúInterface: PluginPackageManager‚Äù topic for more information.</li>
<li>The callbacks.addScript() method can now take a MAXScript function as the callback argument. Previously this argument was a string, stringStream, or file name.</li>
<li>The new Weighted Normals Modifier is exposed in the MAXScript class Weighted_Normals.</li>
<li>All of the ATF-based import plugins have two new properties: importHiddenObjects and preserveLayers.</li>
<li>The Edit_Poly object and Editable_Poly modfier have many new properties and methods exposing the Chamfer updates introduced in previous 2020 releases.</li>
<li>The SME (Slate Material Editor) interface has several new methods for managing Material Libraries.</li>
</ul>
<p>For a list of new features released throughout 3ds Max 2020 Updates, please see <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=GUID-F90290FA-90A2-4720-B9FE-A4CCE0446252">this online help page</a>.</p>

TITLE: Forge Design Automation for 3ds Max went into production on October 28th! Join us for a webinar to learn more.
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: forge-design-automation-for-3ds-max-went-into-production-on-october-28th-join-us-for-a-webinar-to-le
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: Announcement
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: Cloud Service
CATEGORY: Design Automation
CATEGORY: Event
CATEGORY: Forge

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2019/12/forge-design-automation-for-3ds-max-went-into-production-on-october-28th-join-us-for-a-webinar-to-le.html 
DATE: 12/05/2019 03:11:36 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Have you heard?! Forge Design Automation for 3ds Max went into production on October 28<sup>th</sup>. To learn more about this service and how you can batch process your 3ds Max tasks, check out the webinar series here: <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/blog/design-automation-api-webinar-series-register-now">https://forge.autodesk.com/blog/design-automation-api-webinar-series-register-now</a>. You can register for the 3ds Max webinar, as well as the other Design Automation engines (including AutoCAD, Revit, and Inventor).</p>
<p>What can you do with 3ds Max Design Automation? Any sort of automated processing! 3ds Max desktop software already includes a tool called 3ds Max Batch. This tool allows local automation of tasks and is a good way to test your automation before using the Design Automation system. See here for the 3ds Max 2020 Batch details: <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=GUID-0968FF0A-5ADD-454D-B8F6-1983E76A4AF9">http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=GUID-0968FF0A-5ADD-454D-B8F6-1983E76A4AF9</a></p>
<p>Anything that runs in the 3ds Max Batch tool is possible to run in the 3ds Max Design Automation engine. You can also include plug-ins that can be automated. Typically, you would provide a MAXScript that would execute the automation, but the code itself could live in a C++ or a .NET plug-in. Of course, the MAXScript could also contain the automation code. The Design Automation API also supports the ability to pass parameters into the script code, that can also be passed into the automation code. This will allow very flexible workflows with the ability to provide configurations and data to the automation job. For example, you could have a configurator website that takes information from your customer, then using 3ds Max Design Automation you could auto-generate a max model to give back to your customer. Using other Forge APIs, you could also preview the model using the Forge Model Derivative service and the Forge Viewer.</p>
<p><img src="https://adndevblog.typepad.com/.a/6a0167607c2431970b0240a4cb2a25200d-pi" /></p>

<h3>3ds Max Design Automation tutorials and samples</h3>
<p>The engineering product team has produced a step-by-step tutorial that our docs team recently published. Check it out <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/en/docs/design-automation/v3/tutorials/3dsmax/">here</a>. Design Automation V3 is still listed in beta, but we have had a lot of great feedback for the three new engines: Inventor, Revit and 3ds Max. Because we are still in beta, remember when browsing into the V3 docs you will have to pay attention to version. For example, when going into the Developer&#39;s Guide, you will typically land <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/en/docs/design-automation/v2/developers_guide/overview/">here</a>. For the beta version 3, change the v2-&gt;v3 and you&#39;ll come into the new docs. Also notice there are new step-by-step guides for Revit and Inventor. This content will change throughout the beta cycle, so come back regularly and don&#39;t be surprised to find more improvements and changes here in coming weeks.</p>
<p>A couple of things to note... This step-by-step tutorial is currently showing 3ds Max 2019 as an example. Currently 2018, 2019 and 2020 are all available. We have two other resources for .NET Core/ASP <a href="https://github.com/kevinvandecar/design.automation.3dsmax-csharp-meshoptimizer">here</a> and as part of the &quot;Learn Forge&quot; site <a href="https://learnforge.autodesk.io/#/tutorials/modifymodels">here</a>. Both of those are using 3ds Max 2020 (and the .NET plugin needs 2020, unless you make a few code changes. (Ping me if you need help)). One of our engineering guys also has a nice postman tutorial <a href="https://github.com/Developer-Autodesk/design.automation.3dsmax-postman-tutorial">here</a>.&#0160; I am also considering to move the &quot;<a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry">explode geometry</a>&quot; app store example to 3ds Max Design Automation. Is there anyone out there who has other ideas for design automation activities? If so, feel free to comment below, or send me email.</p>
<h3>SIGGRAPH 2019</h3>
<p>SIGGRAPH 2019 is also only a week away. If you are planning to attend, the Forge ADN DevTech M&amp;E team will be there! <a href="https://twitter.com/kevinvandecar">Myself</a>, Chen Xi Li, <a href="https://twitter.com/Apprentice3d">Denis Grigor,</a> and <a href="https://twitter.com/lanhhong">Lanh Hong</a> will be in the Autodesk booth during the week demoing Forge topics, including Forge Design Automation for 3ds Max. We also have a <a href="https://s2019.siggraph.org/session/?sess=sess461">talk during the Autodesk Sponsored Vision series</a>. For the full Autodesk agenda check out <a href="https://area.autodesk.com/events/siggraph2019/">here</a>. We will be in the Autodesk booth during the following exhibition hours: Tues 11-12, 2-3, 5-6; Wed 11-12, 2-3, 5-6; Thur 11-12, 2-3. Stop by and say hi! Hope to see you there!</p>

TITLE: Announcing 3ds Max 2020! - Customization Update
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: announcing-3ds-max-2020-customization-updates

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2019/03/announcing-3ds-max-2020-customization-updates.html 
DATE: 03/29/2019 10:55:05 AM
-----
BODY:
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0240a44c70b4200c-pi"><img alt="3dsMax2020_header_image" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c0240a44c70b4200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c0240a44c70b4200c-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="3dsMax2020_header_image" /></a><br /><br />On Wednesday 3ds Max 2020 started to roll out to customers and partners. The most important news is that 3ds Max 2020 is a binary breaking release and bumps the developer environment to Visual Studio 2017, so C++ plugins will need to be minimally recompiled. There was not a lot of change to the SDK, so rebuilding should not be an issue.</p>
<p>To start, it&#39;s important to know what came into 3ds Max during the 2019 cycle, which is of course all included in the 20202 release. Here is a list of links to feature updates that came from 2019 Update 1 through 3ds Max 2020.</p>
<h3>Feature Updates</h3>
<ul>
<li>What‚Äôs new in 3ds Max 2019 Update 1 <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=GUID-74C66EC8-5B23-429F-8DD5-89791B8C11A4">here </a></li>
<li>What‚Äôs new in 3ds Max 2019 Update 2 <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=GUID-8ED9B0EB-D581-4DCD-8125-B7171AB1B2B6">here </a></li>
<li>What‚Äôs new in 3ds Max 2019 Update 3 <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=GUID-A3A1B7B4-FFA3-4314-AE8B-448E45DFC499">here </a></li>
<li>What‚Äôs new in 3ds Max 2020 <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=GUID-2958CAB3-3C80-40AF-969E-BF23AB4296A5">here</a></li>
<li>Also see the current AREA new feature blogs <a href="https://area.autodesk.com/blogs/the-3ds-max-blog/">here</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3>Plugin Package Format (aka App Store bundle format)</h3>
<p>The 3ds Max product team also released a Forge 3ds Max Design Automation engine into beta last fall. See <a href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2018/12/forge-3ds-max-design-automation-is-in-public-beta.html">here</a> for that info. The Plugin Package Format is an important aspect of the 3ds Max DA functionality, but it also extends to the entire 3ds Max product (3ds Max, 3dsmaxbatch, and 3ds Max DA). If you are someone who customizes 3ds Max, especially as a commercial developer, or a tools developer, where you need to redistribute the customization routines/plugins, this format can be very helpful. It is completely independent of the 3ds max install and profile locations. You can place this anywhere, and 3ds Max can be configured to use it and as a default location as well. It also helps you to keep your file set in a standalone folder structure.</p>
<p>Changes to Plugin Package format for 3ds Max 2020 are mentioned <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2020_sdk_html">here</a>&#0160;in the change listing. One thing to note is that <code>UpgradeCode</code> is now a required value. This help ensures there are no clashes between like-named packages. Make sure to read the important changes to that aspect. Packages without an <code>UpgradeCode</code> will not load in 3ds Max 2020 (but did in prior releases). The package format and MSI that are generated for the App Store are using Microsoft standards (see <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/desktop/msi/upgradecode">here</a>). The <code>UpgradeCode</code> is explained in greater detail there. See these sections for complete details:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2020_sdk_html">3ds Max 2020 Plugin Package changes</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_writing_plug_ins_packaging_plugins_packaging_plugins_html">Packaging Plugins</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_writing_plug_ins_packaging_plugins_packagexml_format_html">Plugin Package Format</a></li>
<li><a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_writing_plug_ins_packaging_plugins_packagexml_example_html">Plugin Package Example</a></li>
</ul>
<p>We also have two examples showing this Plugin Package Format for the Autodesk App Store:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Bake-Radiosity">https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Bake-Radiosity</a> (C++ utility plugin)</li>
<li><a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry">https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-Explode-Geometry</a> (.NET plugin)</li>
</ul>
<p>This format is used by any of the applications that are supported in the App Store. This means products like Revit, AutoCAD, and Inventor all use this format as well. If you are developing apps for other products, it can be helpful to manage all the apps in a similar way. Of course there are some product specific features, but the overall idea is the same. 3ds Max, Revit, Inventor, and AutoCAD all now have Forge Design Automation engines as well, so a lot of possibility!</p>
<h3>What‚Äôs new in the 3ds Max 2020 SDK</h3>
<p>For all the changes in 3ds Max 2020 SDK, see <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2020_sdk_html">here</a>.&#0160;</p>
<h4>Important Details for C++ developers!</h4>
<p>For complete SDK requirements, see <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_about_the_3ds_max_sdk_sdk_requirements_html">here.</a></p>
<p>SDK Break</p>
<p>The 3ds Max 2020 SDK is not binary backward compatible with the 3ds Max 2019 SDK. Plugins will need to be re-compiled to work in 3ds Max 2020.</p>
<p>Microsoft Visual Studio 2017</p>
<p>3ds Max 2020 has been compiled with Microsoft Visual Studio 2017 version 15.8.3, Platform Toolset v141. The Windows Platform SDK version is 10.0.17134.0. Plugins need to be built using the same Platform Toolset version. Any version of Microsoft Visual Studio can be used where the main requirement is to use the Platform Toolset v141. Although other Platform SDK versions may work, it is also suggested to use 10.0.17134.0. The SDK property sheets refer to this, so if you change to a newer version or some reason, you will have to update the property sheet.</p>
<p>Qt Framework</p>
<p>3ds Max 2020 is based on Qt 5.11.2. Although Qt guarantees that minor releases are binary and source backward compatible, we recommend using the same Qt version as 3ds Max uses for plugin development.&#0160; Qt Support for parameter blocks-based UI and also the Plugin Wizard has been added.</p>
<p>Other highlights</p>
<p>Recently 3ds Max switched from ‚Äúfast math‚Äù to ‚Äúprecise math‚Äù compiler settings. There is an interesting MS blog article that explains the differences <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/vcblog/2015/10/19/do-you-prefer-fast-or-precise/">here</a>.&#0160;&#0160;</p>
<p>3ds Max 2020 also adds OSL Shader API for 3rd party renderers.</p>
<p>If you are developing Modifiers, make sure to see the <strong>Modifier Plugin Class Changes to Support Pb1 to Pb2 Migration</strong> section of SDK changes. There were also two new functions added to help find nodes from within the Modifier APIs.</p>
<p>Make sure to review the entire article here for complete 3ds Max 202 SDK changes, <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2020_sdk_html">here</a>.&#0160;</p>
<h3>MAXScript</h3>
<p>Again, there were several changes made during the 2019 cycle. For those details, see <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=GUID-0890917F-5AC9-4E01-B860-0095172B48A9">here</a>.&#0160;</p>
<p>For 3ds Max 2020, all the changes are listed <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2020/ENU/?guid=GUID-F90290FA-90A2-4720-B9FE-A4CCE0446252">here</a>. One thing to note, is that to support the Plugin Package format and changes, the <code>ExchangeStorePackageManager</code> has been renamed to <code>PluginPackageManager</code>. The old name will continue to work as a global variable, but I would encourage you to get used to the new name for the overall system.</p>
<h3>Python</h3>
<p>The Python version used by 3ds Max has been upgraded to 2.7.15. The Pyside2 version included with 3ds Max is updated to 5.11.2.</p>
<p>The pymxs docs (starting in 2019.3) are being updated to add more examples, and explanation of how to handle edge cases and known issues.</p>
<h3>.NET API</h3>
<p>There were no changes to the .NET API, and .NET Framework remains at 4.7</p>

TITLE: Forge 3ds Max Design Automation is in public Beta!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1

BASENAME: forge-3ds-max-design-automation-is-in-public-beta

DATE: 12/03/2018 08:21:39 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>At Forge DevCon 2018 in Las Vegas a few weeks ago, we announced the Forge 3ds Max Design Automation service is now available in beta. Find the main announcement here: <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/blog/forge-3ds-max-design-automation-public-beta">https://forge.autodesk.com/blog/forge-3ds-max-design-automation-public-beta</a>.&#0160;</p>
<p>What is Forge Design Automation? Well it allows you to run automation jobs in the Forge cloud services, and make use of cloud processing. This allows all sorts of options! From commercial configurator type websites, to internal company automation processing that frees up local licenses for real work. :-)</p>
<p>If you are not familiar with Autodesk Forge cloud services, see here: <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/">https://forge.autodesk.com/</a></p>
<p>If you do not have any prior Forge experience, to get started, I would recommend going through some of the basic tutorials first. These can be found here: <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/developer/getting-started">https://forge.autodesk.com/developer/getting-started</a>. The account setup and OAuth authentication APIs are the same for all Forge services. Once you have that basic understanding, then you can follow the <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/blog/forge-3ds-max-design-automation-public-beta">Forge blog announcement post</a>&#0160;to get started with a <a href="https://github.com/Autodesk-Forge/design.automation.3dsmax-nodejs-basic">3ds Max Design Automation sample</a> that uses NodeJS.&#0160;</p>
<p>If you are interested in the Forge related classes at Autodesk University, check it out here: <a href="https://autode.sk/2DX54B0">Forge AU Classes</a>, and see here for all the <a href="https://autode.sk/2APk0Ot">3ds Max AU Classes</a>.&#0160;</p>
<p>Just think of all the possibilities for using Design Automation!&#0160;</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad3c4a3f3200b-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="3dsMaxDA" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c022ad3c4a3f3200b image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad3c4a3f3200b-800wi" title="3dsMaxDA" /></a></p>

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2018/10/forge-devcon-2018-coming-to-au-las-vegas-nov1213.html 
DATE: 10/03/2018 10:10:45 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>&#0160;<a class="asset-img-link" href="https://forge.autodesk.com/devcon-2018" style="float: right;"><img alt="2018-10-03_0946_blog" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c022ad36ff942200c img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36ff942200c-320wi" style="margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="2018-10-03_0946_blog" /></a></p>
<p>If you are planning to come to Autodesk University, or if just interested in the Forge APIs, then the <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/devcon-2018">Forge DevCon</a> is something you should attend. Remember early bird ends October, 15 and you can&#0160;<a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/devcon-2018#tickets">register</a> for AU and/or DevCon today.</p>
<p>DevCon is occurring conveniently on November 12+13 adjacent to Autodesk University. There are ~35 Forge DevCon classes scheduled on&#0160;<a href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/loading.ww?redirectUrl=%2Fconnect%2Fsearch.ww%23loadSearch-searchPhrase%3D%26searchType%3Dsession%26tc%3D0%26sortBy%3DdayTime%26i%2859817%29%3D448340%26dayID%3D11085%26i%2841005%29%3D%26i%2857245%29%3D%26p%3D" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Monday</a>&#0160;November 12 and&#0160;<a href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/loading.ww?redirectUrl=%2Fconnect%2Fsearch.ww%23loadSearch-searchPhrase%3DAS225026%2BSD225601%2BSD231762%2BSD195763%2BSD223996%2BAS226079%2BCS226835%2BSD226781%2BSD224712%2BFDC231765%2BFDC226973%26searchType%3Dsession%26tc%3D0%26sortBy%3Drelevance%26i%2841005%29%3D%26i%2857245%29%3D%26p%3D%0A" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Tuesday</a>&#0160;November 13<sup>th</sup>. Also note that Forge DevCon will overlay the <a href="https://au.autodesk.com/las-vegas/connect-construct-summit">Connect and Construct</a> summit and there is an option to purchase of a two-day DevCon pass allowing you to attend both Monday/Tuesday content, including the AU keynote, DevLab, and Expo on Tuesday, without purchasing a full AU conference pass.</p>
<p>Denis and I will be teaching a class as well. A good chance to come by and meet us! Our class <a href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=226781">SD226781 ‚Äì Advanced Techniques for Using the Forge Viewer</a>,&#0160;will be on Tuesday morning. Of course there will be a variety of other courses including these interesting ones:&#0160;<a href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=223617">CS223617 - A Tinkerer&#39;s Experience Getting Off the Ground with Forge</a>,&#0160;<a class="openInPopup" href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=223831"><span class="abbreviation">FDC223831 -&#0160;</span><span class="title">Move to Forge and the Cloud With Your Existing .NET Experience</span></a>,&#0160;<a class="openInPopup" href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=231761"><span class="abbreviation">FDC231761 -&#0160;</span><span class="title">The Future of Forge: An overview of the Evolution of the Forge Platform</span></a>, and&#0160;<a class="openInPopup" href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=196412"><span class="abbreviation">FDC196412 -&#0160;</span><span class="title">Creating Flexible Offline Workflows Using Autodesk Forge</span></a>.&#0160;</p>
<p>We will also be around in the Forge Village/Expo on Monday. In the Village (again shared with Connect and Construct) there will be technology showcases, including an AR VR area. We will demonstrate some AR and VR technology using the <a href="http://forgetoolkit.com/#/">Forge toolkit</a>. The toolkit currently supports Unity, and they will be a sponsor at AU this year, including having a booth in the Forge Village. Here is a related class:&#0160;<a class="openInPopup" href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=225860"><span class="abbreviation">SD225860 -&#0160;</span><span class="title">Hit the Ground Running with Unity and Forge.<mark class="searchHighlight"></mark></span></a></p>
<p>Why are we discussing this in a 3ds Max developer blog? Well... APIs are APIs! but, more importantly the 3ds Max (*.max) format is now supported in the <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/en/docs/model-derivative/v2/developers_guide/supported-translations/">Forge Model Derivative </a>service. For some supporting details about how the *.max translations work, see&#0160;some tips by Denis on our <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/blog/control-default-view-when-translating-3ds-max-files">Forge blog</a>&#0160;and on&#0160;<a href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/49245354/3ds-max-textures-custom-materials/49411624#49411624">stackoverflow</a>.&#0160;Moreover, the recent 3ds Max <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=GUID-80F02417-2CDB-42B8-88E5-86E6DD91C71E">Shared Views </a>feature is powered by Forge, and Forge DevCon is an excellent opportunity to understand how you can also use these parts and build for 3ds Max. You can understand how the Shared Views works and how to create a similar experience on your own web site. In addition to the <a href="https://forge.autodesk.com/api/design-automation-cover-page/">AutoCAD Design Automation,</a> you will hear about new <a href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=226894" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Design Automation for Revit</a>&#0160;and&#0160;<a href="https://autodeskuniversity.smarteventscloud.com/connect/sessionDetail.ww?SESSION_ID=225569" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Design Automation for&#0160;Inventor</a>&#0160;services. With those clearly on the horizon, I can only guess that 3ds Max Design Automation will be coming soon. :-)</p>
<p>Hope to see you there!</p>

TITLE: 3ds Max Public Debug Symbols - Updated with complete instructions
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: 3ds-max-public-debug-symbols-updated
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: debug

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2018/09/3ds-max-public-debug-symbols-updated.html 
DATE: 09/18/2018 10:03:23 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Hi All, Almost 5 years ago, I wrote the original article here about public debug symbols. I had some recent questions about debug symbols and realized that a link in the original article was not working, so wanted to complete the whole story here again. Autodesk 3ds Max is a unique product in the company&#39;s portfolio. The engineering team for 3ds Max is keen on helping the developer community as much as possible. With that, they are providing 3ds Max debug symbols via an online symbol server. These are public symbols that are stripped, so there is no source code information. However, the symbols can show you very quickly were a problem may be coming from, especially given the many different ways you can derive C++ plugins and utilize the virtual callbacks from 3ds Max.</p>
<p>This article describes the steps to setup and use the symbols to get extra call stack details when debugging. To setup the Visual Studio to use the public symbol server, first click the debug menu and choose options. Then follow these steps in the Debug Options dialog:</p>
<ol>
<li>In the left list, choose Debugging -&gt; Symbols</li>
<li>Click the folder Icon in upper right</li>
<li>In the blank space added, enter&#0160;http://symbols.autodesk.com/symbols , and make sure the check box is checked.</li>
<li>If you want to store the symbols offline in a different location from default, enter the location in the &quot;Cache Symbols in this directory&quot;</li>
<li>Select the &quot;All Modules, unless excluded&quot; option to load all the 3ds Max modules during a debug session. Note this applies to all the symbol locations checked. For example, the default includes Microsoft Symbol Servers, so those will also load as needed. You can hone this down by using the &quot;Only specified modules&quot; but it takes more time to setup and figure out. You can also check/uncheck the symbol servers as a whole to control other servers (like uncheck Microsoft Symbol Servers) if you only want to use 3ds Max symbols.<br /><br />See the below screen capture:<a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36c35c8200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Debug01" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c022ad36c35c8200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36c35c8200c-800wi" title="Debug01" /></a></li>
</ol>
<p>After the setup, you can set breakpoints, and then start debugging. First, remember that even though we are debugging a plugin in 3ds Max, using the production version, we need to use the &quot;hybrid&quot; configuration so that the various run-times are production, and not debug. When starting 3ds Max in a hybrid debug mode, you will see in the output window whether the symbols are loading for each module. For example:</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36c3669200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Debug02" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c022ad36c3669200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36c3669200c-800wi" title="Debug02" /></a></p>
<p>After 3ds Max is fully started, you can now start debugging and you can stop in break points within your plugin, and if 3ds Max symbols have call stack information in the context of your debugging session, it will be displayed in the call stack window. For example, in a basic UtilityObj plugin, during the BeginEditParams routine, you can get the following enhanced call stack:</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad3925f04200d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Debug3" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c022ad3925f04200d image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad3925f04200d-800wi" title="Debug3" /></a></p>
<p>Without the symbols being loaded, the same location will look like below, and you will only see memory locations.</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36c36ec200c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Debug4" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c022ad36c36ec200c image-full img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c022ad36c36ec200c-800wi" title="Debug4" /></a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>When public symbols first became available, FCS symbols were the only versions uploaded, but since around 2015, update versions have also been included. The symbol server should always contain all public releases with matching symbols. If you run into trouble about symbols loading, make sure all the options are correct, and after double checking if they are not loading, feel free to ping me and I can double-check they are present on the symbol server.&#0160;</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Hope it helps! Happy Fall!</p>
-----

TITLE: Introducing 3ds Max 2019 and SDK Changes
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: introducing-3ds-max-2019-and-sdk-changes
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: Announcement
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: DevDocs
CATEGORY: MAXScript
CATEGORY: Python

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2018/03/introducing-3ds-max-2019-and-sdk-changes.html 
DATE: 03/22/2018 03:51:13 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>3ds max 2019 is coming very soon! You can find the help is now online, with the <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=GUID-40222876-7E08-42F8-A912-F6CDC597A3FD">new features discussed here</a>. If you are a subscriber, you should see it listed in <a href="https://manage.autodesk.com">https://manage.autodesk.com</a> soon (if not already there).</p>
<p>One of the first things you will notice is that 3ds Max 2019 is introducing support for the Open Shading Language (OSL). We have already started a github repo that will allow community members to share and contribute shaders. See here:&#0160;<a href="https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-OSL-Shaders">https://github.com/ADN-DevTech/3dsMax-OSL-Shaders</a>.&#0160;For the overview and 3ds Max specific information pertaining to OSL shaders, see here: <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__developer_3ds_max_sdk_features_rendering_osl_html">Open Shading Language (OSL) Support</a>. Also check out the general OSL github repo and docs <a href="https://github.com/imageworks/OpenShadingLanguage/#introduction">here</a>.</p>
<p>Make sure to check out this AREA blog article announcing 3ds Max 2019: <br /> <a href="https://area.autodesk.com/blogs/the-3ds-max-blog/meet-3ds-max-2019/">https://area.autodesk.com/blogs/the-3ds-max-blog/meet-3ds-max-2019/</a></p>
<p>From the SDK perspective,&#0160;this release is again a binary breaking release. Although the SDK itself did not change too much, you will have to recompile your plugins. The same development environment is specified as was in 2018, so mainly Microsoft Visual Studio 2015 Update 3, Platform Toolset v140, and Windows SDK 10.0.10586. Due to some new components, the .NET Framework is bumped to 4.7 and now Qt 5.6.3 or 5.6.2 can be used. See <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__developer_about_the_3ds_max_sdk_sdk_requirements_html">SDK Requirements here</a> for complete details.</p>
<p>Highlights from the SDK changes include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Improved support for loading binary dependencies (DLLs in same folder as plug-in)</li>
<li>Support for Autodesk Application Plug-in Packages, this is the same structure that the Autodesk App store uses</li>
<li>Improved parameter block validation</li>
<li>Improved support for saving to previous scene file versions of PB1 plugins migrated to PB2</li>
<li>Thread Safe EvalXXX Methods improvements</li>
<li>Vertex Velocity Interface</li>
<li>New Double precision geometric primitives</li>
</ul>
<p>For complete details, please see: <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2019_sdk_html">What&#39;s New: 3ds Max 2019 SDK</a>.&#0160;</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Highlights from the MAXScript environment include:</p>
<ul>
<li>OSL Suport</li>
<li>Shape Booleans</li>
<li>Improvements to the Alembic import and export plug-ins are exposed to MAXScript</li>
</ul>
<p>For complete details, please see: <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2019/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_0890917F_5AC9_4E01_B860_0095172B48A9_htm">What&#39;s New in MAXScript in 3ds Max 2019</a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The Python version used by 3ds Max continues to be 2.7.12.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The .NET SDK now requires .NET Framework 4.7. There were minor bugs fixed here again, to help cleanup this environment.</p>
<p>That‚Äôs it for now! Enjoy 3ds Max 2019!</p>
-----

TITLE: Updated .NET API Samples for 3ds Max 2018
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: updated-net-api-samples-for-3ds-max-2018
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: Samples
CATEGORY: WPF

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2017/10/updated-net-api-samples-for-3ds-max-2018.html 
DATE: 10/05/2017 03:53:27 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Well, it&#39;s been a while since last posting, but trying to do more. Recently someone asked about the .NET API for recent versions of 3ds Max. There has really been no big changes for a few releases except moving from ParamBlock1 to ParamBlock2 for some of the older geometry objects and modifiers. .NET API, plus WPF, etc. still work OK, even though the main 3ds Max UI is moving to Qt. To demonstrate, I updated the samples I provided back in 2014 release to work with 2018. These are the things I changed to get everything working well again:</p>
<ul>
<li>Update the csproj variables to use the 3ds Max values (Currently: $(ADSK_3DSMAX_x64_2018)). Note the original project used: $(ADSK_MAXDES_x64_2014), but 3ds Max Design as not been available for several releases now, and is combined with 3ds Max as a workspace. That makes it easier to handle 3ds Max plugin projects! The variable changes are for the assembly references, and also for the Post-Build event command line, that provides the copy operation.</li>
<li>The .NET Target framework should move to at least 4.6 to match the version 3ds Max itself is using.</li>
<li>In the code, there was one place where we fixed a defect in Autodesk.Max.dll. Line #119 of HelixControl.xaml.cs was using the (IntPtr) cast for the IINodeTab value. We fixed that API to properly use an integer index, so the cast is no longer required.</li>
<li>Updated a screen bitmap for the CreateTeapotUserControl</li>
<li>Fixed the teapot creation in CreateTeapotUserControl... turns out it was updated with the move to ParamBlock2. Added a comment to show this.</li>
<li>Added a tiny error check for the &quot;05 - Create Face Objects&quot; routine to ensure the user picks something before continuing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Overall, pretty minor changes...I have attached the updated sample here: <span class="asset  asset-generic at-xid-6a019104a31725970c01bb09ca58fb970d img-responsive"><a href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/files/adncuisamples_blogv2018-1.zip">AdnCuiSamples_BlogV2018</a></span>.</p>
<p>Enjoy!</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>

TITLE: 3ds Max 2018 SDK Changes
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: 3ds-max-2018-sdk-changes
CATEGORY: .NET API
CATEGORY: Announcement
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: MAXScript
CATEGORY: Python
CATEGORY: qt

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2017/04/3ds-max-2018-sdk-changes.html 
DATE: 04/12/2017 01:34:15 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Another year has passed, and we have a new release of 3ds Max! 3ds Max 2018 was released today, and should be available soon in your Autodesk Account access. The online help is also already rolled out.For new features, see <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2018/ENU/?guid=GUID-F687E23D-6FBA-4C8A-9202-C30F2860E5BE">What&#39;s New in 3ds Max 2018</a>.</p>
<p>For the 3ds Max SDK changes, see&#0160; <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2018/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2018_sdk_html">What&#39;s New: 3ds Max 2018 SDK</a>. As in the past, the SDK is included in the install folder structure. Typically, it is here: .\x64\Tools\MAXSDK\SDK_3dsMax2018.msi</p>
<h3>Some SDK highlights:</h3>
<p>The first thing to note from the C++ programming perspective, is that the compiler has been bumped to Visual Studio 2015 <strong>update 3</strong>. You are probably already there with Visual Studio 2015, but be sure to check and update to ensure compatibility. Even though 3ds Max 2017 was using Visual Studio 2015 (RTM), you will have to rebuild any plugins. The 3ds Max 2018 release is not binary compatible with 2017.</p>
<p>Qt is also majorly bumped in 3ds Max 2018 and is now using Qt 5.6.2.</p>
<p>You will also notice that all the samples in the SDK have been updated to use the Parameter Block 2 standard. There&#39;s a new <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2018/ENU/?guid=__developer_3ds_max_sdk_features_working_with_plug_ins_parameter_blocks_pb1_to_pb2_conversion_html">Parameter Block Porting Guide</a> in the docs. Part of this is to encourage everyone with Parameter Block 1 definitions, to move to Parameter Block 2. In the future the old Parameter block 1 will be deprecated.</p>
<p>Two new features that came recently are the Data Channel Modifier, and the Bezier Trajectories. Both have some new SDK access in the 3ds Max 2018 SDK. Additionally, there were some minor UI API changes, and also around the Rendering APIs. See the <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2018/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_what_s_new_3ds_max_2018_sdk_html">help</a> for details.</p>
<h3>Other programming environments:</h3>
<p>For 3ds Max 2018 MAXScript changes, check-out <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2018/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_1AB01BA7_7337_4E2F_8CFE_E0AB55EFE995_htm">What&#39;s New in MAXScript in 3ds Max 2018</a>.</p>
<p>For 3ds Max 2018 Python changes, check-out <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2018/ENU/?guid=__developer_what_s_new_in_3ds_max_python_api_what_s_new_in_the_3ds_max_2018_p_html">What&#39;s New in the 3ds Max 2018 Python API</a>.</p>
<p>There were also a few minor changes to the 3ds Max 2018 .NET API assemblies. Mainly cleaning up signatures, and other miscellaneous fixes.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>Happy coding with 3ds Max 2018!</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
-----

AUTHOR: Denis Grigor
AUTHOR EMAIL: denis.grigor@autodesk.com
TITLE: How to properly check if a material is used in a scene?
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: how-to-properly-check-if-a-material-is-used-in-a-scene
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: debug
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2017/04/how-to-properly-check-if-a-material-is-used-in-a-scene.html 
DATE: 04/10/2017 03:32:21 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Sometimes you may need to know if a given material is used within the scene or not. In Compact Material Editor it is usually marked with the UI giving you certain clues. For example, in the screen capture below, the gray corners indicate the material is used in the scene. Corners that are filled in white, indicate the material is used, and also is being used by a selected scene object. The white rectangle indicates it is the currently selected material.</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c01bb0974d5ca970d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c01bb0974d5ca970d img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c01bb0974d5ca970d-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="Image" /></a></p>
<p>The same indicators are found in the Slate Material editor. They will display on the preview of the material.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c01bb098f042b970d-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image (2)" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c01bb098f042b970d img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c01bb098f042b970d-500wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="Image (2)" /></a></p>
<p>&#0160;</p>
<p>The obvious question now is how to retrieve this information using the C++ SDK? Let&#39;s take a look at how to do it.<br /> <br /> The very first step is to have a look at the <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_class_mtl_base_html">MtlBase class</a> where you will notice the<strong><em> int TestMtlFlag(int mask)</em></strong> that&#0160;<em>&quot;Tests the specified flags. Returns nonzero if the flags are set; otherwise zero‚Äù</em>&#0160;. Among the available <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_group__material_flags_html">Materials flags</a> we can notice the <em><strong>MTL_IN_SCENE&#0160;</strong></em>flag, that seems to be exactly what we need.<br /> <br /> Thus, to test if a material is used or not we can easily do:</p>
<div style="font-family: &#39;Roboto Condensed&#39;, Tauri, &#39;Hiragino Sans GB&#39;, &#39;Microsoft YaHei&#39;, STHeiti, SimSun, &#39;Lucida Grande&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans Unicode&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans&#39;, &#39;Segoe UI&#39;, AppleSDGothicNeo-Medium, &#39;Malgun Gothic&#39;, Verdana, Tahoma, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; overflow-x: hidden; overflow-y: auto; margin: 0px !important; padding: 20px; background-color: #ffffff; color: #222222; line-height: 1.6; -webkit-font-smoothing: antialiased; background: #ffffff;">
<pre style="border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; border: 1px solid #cccccc; overflow: auto; padding: 0.5em; display: block; overflow-x: auto; color: #657b83; background: #fdf6e3;"><code class="cpp" data-origin="&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class=&quot;cpp&quot;&gt;if(my_material-&amp;gt;TestMtlFlag(MTL_IN_SCENE))
{
    \\ It is used
}else
{
    \\it is not
}
&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;" style="border: 1px solid #cccccc; display: block; font-family: Consolas, Inconsolata, Courier, monospace; font-weight: bold; white-space: pre; margin: 0px 2px; border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; padding: 0px 5px; font-size: 1em; letter-spacing: -1px;"><span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">if</span>(my_material-&gt;TestMtlFlag(MTL_IN_SCENE))
{
    \\ It is used
} <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">else</span>
{
    \\it is not
}
</code></pre>
</div>
<p>Hurrah! Job is done, let&#39;s go home.<br /> <br /> Not so fast.<br /> <br />The <strong>MTL_IN_SCENE</strong> flag is useful only if somebody sets this flag (calling <em>MtlBase::SetMtlFlag</em>), but it turns out that nobody sets this specific flag, like ever. Thus, it will always return 0, no matter what, and even if you have assigned this material to dozens of objects in the scene, it is never accurate, unless someone sets it (maybe you set it in your plugin, but is seems none of the default materials are doing this.)<br /> <br /> Other <em>(Materials)</em> flags seems to be working fine, thus being useful, but not this one. So, let&#39;s get back to work.<br /> <br /> This question is not new, and there are lot of <em>(mostly MAXScript)</em> recipes on how to check whenever a given material is used somewhere in the scene, and the common algorithm is to get the scene materials and check if the material in question is found among them.<br /> <br /> That should be piece of cake, as the <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_class_interface_html">Interface Class</a> offers us the <strong><em>GetSceneMtls</em></strong> method, and the returned <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_class_mtl_base_lib_html">MtlBaseLib</a> has the handy <em><strong>FindMaterial</strong></em> method for finding a material by name:</p>
<div style="font-family: &#39;Roboto Condensed&#39;, Tauri, &#39;Hiragino Sans GB&#39;, &#39;Microsoft YaHei&#39;, STHeiti, SimSun, &#39;Lucida Grande&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans Unicode&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans&#39;, &#39;Segoe UI&#39;, AppleSDGothicNeo-Medium, &#39;Malgun Gothic&#39;, Verdana, Tahoma, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; overflow-x: hidden; overflow-y: auto; margin: 0px !important; padding: 20px; background-color: #ffffff; color: #222222; line-height: 1.6; -webkit-font-smoothing: antialiased; background: #ffffff;">
<pre style="border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; border: 1px solid #cccccc; overflow: auto; padding: 0.5em; display: block; overflow-x: auto; color: #657b83; background: #fdf6e3;"><code class="cpp" data-origin="&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class=&quot;cpp&quot;&gt;bool materialIsUsed(MtlBase* this_material)
{
   MtlBaseLib* scene_materials = GetCOREInterface()-&amp;gt;GetSceneMtls();

   return (scene_materials-&amp;gt;FindMtl(this_material) != -1) ? true : false;
}
&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;" style="border: 1px solid #cccccc; display: block; font-family: Consolas, Inconsolata, Courier, monospace; font-weight: bold; white-space: pre; margin: 0px 2px; border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; padding: 0px 5px; font-size: 1em; letter-spacing: -1px;"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">bool</span> <span class="hljs-title" style="color: #268bd2;">materialIsUsed</span><span class="hljs-params">(MtlBase* this_material)</span>
</span>{
   MtlBaseLib* scene_materials = GetCOREInterface()-&gt;GetSceneMtls();

   <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">return</span> (scene_materials-&gt;FindMtl(this_material) != -<span class="hljs-number" style="color: #2aa198;">1</span>) ? <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">true</span> : <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">false</span>;
}
</code></pre>
</div>
<p>Easy say, easy do - can we go home now?<br />Not yet ... not yet ...<br /> <br />It turns out that this approach is not very reliable <em>(noticed by many developers)</em>, and the reason is that there is no dynamic tracking of the materials in the scene, thus the material library returned by the<em><strong> Interface::GetSceneMtls</strong></em> might not contain the latest information.<br /> <br /> There is a way to manually reset and rebuilding the scene lib, but unfortunately it is available <u>only</u> in MAXScript as ‚Äò<strong><em>UpdateSceneMaterialLib()</em></strong>‚Äômethod, and there is not yet a C++ SDK equivalent.<br /> <br /> <em>&quot;So, what it is the big deal? We can execute MAXScript from C++, we can live with that.&quot;</em><br /> <br /> Well ... there is yet another problem.<br /> <br /> If the material in question is a part of a sub-material, then you can check in the scene materials lib whenever you want, it will not show up, because <em>(in a manner of speaking)</em> it contains only the ‚Äúfirst level‚Äù materials and will not contain the materials that are part/contained in other materials (g.e. multi-material).<br /> <br /> <em>‚ÄúThen, what could be the solution?‚Äù</em><br /> <br /> The solution is given us by the <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_C11C8544_C5D5_4BA4_81A7_B00E8F508A03_htm">Reference System</a>, because if we look at MtlBase inheritance diagram:</p>
<p><a class="asset-img-link" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c01b8d25bfecf970c-pi" style="display: inline;"><img alt="Image (1)" border="0" class="asset  asset-image at-xid-6a019104a31725970c01b8d25bfecf970c img-responsive" src="https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/.a/6a019104a31725970c01b8d25bfecf970c-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="Image (1)" /></a></p>
<p>we notice the obvious aspect, that any material <em>(like many other classes in 3ds Max SDK)</em> is also a <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_class_reference_target_html">Reference Target</a>. <br /> <br /> This is obvious, because logically, a material has to have dependents, that are notified upon change <em>(i.e. change the diffuse color)</em>.<br /> <br /> Thus, what is left is to iterate through these dependents, using the dedicated <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_class_dependent_iterator_html">DependentIterator Class</a> and recursively check the dependents.<br /> <br /> Easy say, but not so obviously done:</p>
<div style="font-family: &#39;Roboto Condensed&#39;, Tauri, &#39;Hiragino Sans GB&#39;, &#39;Microsoft YaHei&#39;, STHeiti, SimSun, &#39;Lucida Grande&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans Unicode&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans&#39;, &#39;Segoe UI&#39;, AppleSDGothicNeo-Medium, &#39;Malgun Gothic&#39;, Verdana, Tahoma, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; overflow-x: hidden; overflow-y: auto; margin: 0px !important; padding: 20px; background-color: #ffffff; color: #222222; line-height: 1.6; -webkit-font-smoothing: antialiased; background: #ffffff;">
<pre style="border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; border: 1px solid #cccccc; overflow: auto; padding: 0.5em; display: block; overflow-x: auto; color: #657b83; background: #fdf6e3;"><code class="cpp" data-origin="&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class=&quot;cpp&quot;&gt;static bool  isNodeInScene(INode* node)
{
       for (INode* par = node-&amp;gt;GetParentNode();
              par != nullptr;
              node = par, par = node-&amp;gt;GetParentNode()) {
       }
       return node == GetCOREInterface()-&amp;gt;GetRootNode();
}

 static bool isUsedInScene(ReferenceTarget *mt)
{
       DependentIterator di(mt);
       RefMakerHandle rm;

       if (mt-&amp;gt;SuperClassID() == BASENODE_CLASS_ID) {
              return isNodeInScene(static_castINode*&amp;gt;(mt));
       }

       while ((rm = di.Next()) != NULL) {
              if (rm != mt &amp;amp;&amp;amp; rm-&amp;gt;IsRefTarget()
                     &amp;amp;&amp;amp; isUsedInScene(static_castReferenceTarget*&amp;gt;(rm)))
                     return true;
       }
       return false;
}
&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;" style="border: 1px solid #cccccc; display: block; font-family: Consolas, Inconsolata, Courier, monospace; font-weight: bold; white-space: pre; margin: 0px 2px; border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; padding: 0px 5px; font-size: 1em; letter-spacing: -1px;"><span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">bool</span>  <span class="hljs-title" style="color: #268bd2;">isNodeInScene</span><span class="hljs-params">(INode* node)</span>
</span>{
       <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">for</span> (INode* par = node-&gt;GetParentNode();
              par != <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">nullptr</span>;
              node = par, par = node-&gt;GetParentNode()) {
       }
       <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">return</span> node == GetCOREInterface()-&gt;GetRootNode();
}

 <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">bool</span> <span class="hljs-title" style="color: #268bd2;">isUsedInScene</span><span class="hljs-params">(ReferenceTarget *mt)</span>
</span>{
       <span class="hljs-function">DependentIterator <span class="hljs-title" style="color: #268bd2;">di</span><span class="hljs-params">(mt)</span></span>;
       RefMakerHandle rm;

       <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">if</span> (mt-&gt;SuperClassID() == BASENODE_CLASS_ID) {
              <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">return</span> isNodeInScene(static_castINode*&gt;(mt));
       }

       <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">while</span> ((rm = di.Next()) != NULL) {
              <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">if</span> (rm != mt &amp;&amp; rm-&gt;IsRefTarget()
                     &amp;&amp; isUsedInScene(static_castReferenceTarget*&gt;(rm)))
                     <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">return</span> <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">true</span>;
       }
       <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">return</span> <span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">false</span>;
}
</code></pre>
</div>
<p>Thus, to check if a given material is used in the scene or not, it suffice to call:</p>
<div style="font-family: &#39;Roboto Condensed&#39;, Tauri, &#39;Hiragino Sans GB&#39;, &#39;Microsoft YaHei&#39;, STHeiti, SimSun, &#39;Lucida Grande&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans Unicode&#39;, &#39;Lucida Sans&#39;, &#39;Segoe UI&#39;, AppleSDGothicNeo-Medium, &#39;Malgun Gothic&#39;, Verdana, Tahoma, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; overflow-x: hidden; overflow-y: auto; margin: 0px !important; padding: 20px; background-color: #ffffff; color: #222222; line-height: 1.6; -webkit-font-smoothing: antialiased; background: #ffffff;">
<pre style="border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; border: 1px solid #cccccc; overflow: auto; padding: 0.5em; display: block; overflow-x: auto; color: #657b83; background: #fdf6e3;"><code class="cpp" data-origin="&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code class=&quot;cpp&quot;&gt;if(isUsedInScene(my_material))
{
    \\ It is used
}else
{
    \\it is not
}
&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;" style="border: 1px solid #cccccc; display: block; font-family: Consolas, Inconsolata, Courier, monospace; font-weight: bold; white-space: pre; margin: 0px 2px; border-top-left-radius: 3px; border-top-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-right-radius: 3px; border-bottom-left-radius: 3px; word-wrap: break-word; padding: 0px 5px; font-size: 1em; letter-spacing: -1px;"><span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">if</span>(isUsedInScene(my_material))
{
    \\ It is used
}<span class="hljs-keyword" style="color: #859900;">else</span>
{
    \\it is not
}
</code></pre>
</div>
<p>and the cool thing with this approach is that <em>(I guess you already noticed)</em> it can be used with anything that is ‚Äúreferable‚Äù <em>(i.e. is a ReferenceTarget)</em>, and that could be more interesting than just for materials.</p>

TITLE: Querying the 3ds Max version
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: querying-the-3ds-max-version
CATEGORY: C++
CATEGORY: MAXScript
CATEGORY: Tip/Trick

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2017/02/querying-the-3ds-max-version.html 
DATE: 02/01/2017 04:33:36 PM
-----
BODY:
<p>Anyone taking plug-in development seriously has to think about plugin versioning. The 3ds Max C++ SDK documentation offers a lot of<a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_413D6EDB_E80E_4C3D_A33D_DE639B217919_htm"> information on this topic</a>, along with a couple of implementation techniques and some <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_E7D852FF_CC82_4439_AD11_4A1BE4E8E56D_htm">P_VERSION related best practices</a>.<br /> <br /> For 3ds Max version querying, the 3ds Max C++ SDK&#0160;offers (within <em>plugapi.h</em>) some useful macros like:</p>
<pre id="CAaACAwyfr5">GET_MAX_RELEASE(VERSION_3DSMAX)<br />GET_MAX_API_NUM(VERSION_3DSMAX)<br />GET_MAX_SDK_REV(VERSION_3DSMAX)<br />GET_MAX_SDK_NUMREV(VERSION_3DSMAX)</pre>
<p>that can be used to tailor your plugin to different 3ds Max environments and other uses.<br /> <br /> However all these tools are updated/adjusted with each major 3ds Max release when the 3ds Max SDK is updated, and not with the service packs, extensions, or updates. </p>
<div data-section-style="11" style="max-width: 100%;"><img alt="" height="90" id="CAaACA18liZ" src="https://quip.com/blob/CAaAAAO6TEo/OiQkz4Cax7dsxDZ6WV0_Ew?a=rCQAEJEIaCLj5oveRDVXg4DwdS5zw0KbR1QyDlaTjQsa" width="600" /></div>
<p><br /> This might look irrelevant for a plugin developer, as the C++ SDK is usually binary compatible for a complete full version and sometimes even across main versions (as was the case of 3ds Max 2015 and 2016). Nevertheless, sometimes there is a need to have more details, be it for logging/diagnostic purposes, or to deal with situations when some of your plugin users are not using the latest SP (and are spread between different SP). For these and other cases&#0160;it would be nice to have a way of getting some info on client&#39;s 3ds Max specific version number or build version number and then if necessary, adjust the behavior of your plugin accordingly.<br /> <br /> By inspecting the executable of 3ds Max (3dsmax.exe) we can see that the needed information is included in the file version:</p>
<div data-section-style="11" style="max-width: 100%;"><img alt="" height="516" id="CAaACAIl09M" src="https://quip.com/blob/CAaAAAO6TEo/lMNGpr-TF9o4khnlC8i4Cw?a=Jr38bjstGVgVCEGc6OozywzYoBvoDa4aW5xuCPHFDrEa" width="419" /></div>
<p>where on the above screenshot:19 is the release number corresponding to 3ds Max 2017, 2 is SP number and 420 is the build number.<br /> <br /> To extract this information we could rely on <a href="https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ms647003.aspx">GetFileVersionInfo API</a> (from C++ Windows API) and you can even find some <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/940707/how-do-i-programatically-get-the-version-of-a-dll-or-exe-file">sample code on how to use it</a>&#0160;(thanks to Kevin Vandecar for pointing this out).&#0160;</p>
<p>But in MAXScript, there is a simler way. It turns out that among many <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_BA196B48_8ECA_4E0C_AE2E_F7EFAAF39844_htm">MAXScript external file methods</a>&#0160;there is&#0160;&#0160;<em>getFileVersion</em>&#0160;&lt;filename_string&gt; function:</p>
<pre id="CAaACAod9jd">GetFileVersion (getDir #maxRoot + &quot;\\3dsmax.exe&quot;)<br />--&gt;&#0160;&quot;19,2,420,0 &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160;19,2,420,0&quot;</pre>
<p>that gives us the very information needed.</p>
<p>The fact that it is just a MAXScript function, should not hold us back, as we can easily <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__files_GUID_5CC913A0_E7CC_457B_9EE4_EAA79B8AF2B4_htm">call MAXScript from C++</a>:</p>
<pre id="CAaACAbHhsY">BOOL ExecuteMAXScriptScript(MCHAR *s, BOOL quietErrors = FALSE, FPValue *fpv = NULL);</pre>
<p>and use the extracted information, that in this case will be contained in a <a href="http://help.autodesk.com/view/3DSMAX/2017/ENU/?guid=__cpp_ref_class_f_p_value_html">FPValue</a>:</p>
<pre id="CAaACA8iGUo">#include &lt;maxscript/maxscript.h&gt;<br /><br />int getSPVersion()<br />{<br />&#0160;&#0160; &#0160;FPValue resulted_value;<br />&#0160;&#0160; &#0160;ExecuteMAXScriptScript(L&quot;getFileVersion \&quot;$max/3dsmax.exe\&quot;&quot;, <br />&#0160;&#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160;false, <br />&#0160;&#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160; &#0160;&amp;resulted_value);<br /><br />&#0160;&#0160; &#0160;// WARNING: for illustration only: assumes SP version is 1 digit, 3rd index<br />&#0160;&#0160; &#0160;return static_cast&lt;int&gt;(resulted_value.s[3] - &#39;0&#39;);<br />}</pre>
<p>The MAXScript&#0160;<em>getFileVersion </em>function is in fact using the Windows GetFileVersionInfo API, and this is a very good illustration of how MAXScript is easily inter-operable with the 3ds Max C++ SDK. Either technique frmo the C++ SDK should yeild the same results.</p>
<p>&#0160;Note that due to the recent transition to a subscription-based model, it seems there will be no future <em>Service Packs</em> or <em>Extensions. </em>Instead they will be called <em><strong>Updates</strong></em>. But, using the above described approach, you will still get the desired details. In this most recent example of the 3ds Max 2017 Update, instead of getting a SP version, it will give you the Update version, that can be used for the same purpose.</p>
<p>&#0160;</p>

BODY:
<p>Well, again I find myself apologizing for not posting sooner. In this one, I would like to let you know about the upcoming events we have scheduled pertaining to 3ds Max programming. The first one is at Autodesk University. I will be presenting a new class comparing the differences between Python and the .NET APIs in 3ds Max. Both are relatively new programming features, and both have genuinely different approaches to development. Not just the languages are different! :-) After the classes are presented in person, I will post a few of the details here. Check back in December. Thanks to <a href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/denis-grigor.html">Denis Grigor </a>for helping on the Python content. </p>
<p>This class will be presented in Shanghai, China on Nov. 3 (45 minute version with the help of my colleague, <a href="http://around-the-corner.typepad.com/adn/cheng-xi-li/">Cheng Xi Li</a>), and then again in Las Vegas on Nov. 16 (90 minute version). For information on Autodesk University, see here: <a href="http://au.autodesk.com">au.autodesk.com</a>. If you are attending either event, please come introduce yourself and tell me you read this on the blog!</p>
<p>We will also be holding our annual developer days at several locations around the world in November and December. Although we will not have anything directly pertaining to 3ds Max programming, there will be plenty of topics about related products. The Forge APIs will be a large focus this year. For information about all the different events and the agenda, see here: <a href="http://autodeskdevdays.com/">http://autodeskdevdays.com/</a>. I will be around during the DevLab portion in Las Vegas, so if you have any 3ds Max programming issues, feel free to drop in and see me. Or even if no questions, come by and introduce yourself. :-)</p>
<p>Also, if you have not already, check out the <a href="http://developer.autodesk.com">http://developer.autodesk.com</a> portal where the Forge APIs are available. All you need is an Autodesk ID to login and to create your app.</p>

AUTHOR: Denis Grigor
