TITLE: Welcome to GetCOREInterface!
STATUS: Publish
ALLOW COMMENTS: 1
CONVERT BREAKS: wysiwyg
ALLOW PINGS: 0
BASENAME: welcome-to-the-new-3ds-max-customization-and-programming-blog

UNIQUE URL: https://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/2013/09/welcome-to-the-new-3ds-max-customization-and-programming-blog.html 
DATE: 09/10/2013 11:43:50 AM
-----
BODY:
<p>Welcome to GetCOREInterface! This is a new blog dedicated to 3ds Max customization and programming. It will also have some sprinkling of FBX SDK along with other products relating to 3ds Max and 3ds Max Design. This blog&#0160;will be&#0160;maintained by <a class="zem_slink" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/kevin-vandecar.html" rel="homepage" target="_blank" title="KDV">Kevin Vandecar</a> who is part of&#0160;the Media &amp; Entertainment worldwide team of API gurus providing technical services through the <a class="zem_slink" href="http://www.autodesk.com/adn" rel="homepage" target="_blank" title="ADN">Autodesk Developer Network (ADN)</a>.</p>
<p>Why did I choose GetCOREInterface for the name? Well if you know any basic 3ds Max SDK programming, you know that GetCOREInterface is the entry point API to programming 3ds Max. So why not use it as the entry point for the blog itself? It&#39;s easy to remember and search&#0160;once you become acquainted with programming in 3ds Max. It is also used in the .NET API environment, and it is the underlying access point in MAXScript, too (you just don&#39;t need to know that from a scripting standpoint). That being said, you can expect all forms of programming topics to be covered here including MAXScript, .NET API, and of course the C++ SDK. I will categorize each topic with the primary concepts (.NET API, C++, or MAXScript). But also remember that many techniques can be &quot;ported&quot; to the other environments with minimal effort.</p>
<p>You can expect mostly technical (how-to) solutions and content derived from answering questions from our ADN partners and forum users including sample code.&#0160;I will also provide pointers to&#0160;white papers, screencasts, conference presentation material, and other information derived from our work in ADN. This blog is meant to&#0160;provide up-to-date information, in one place, so you can easily find what you need to solve your programming problems.</p>
<p>For more about me, see here: <a class="zem_slink" href="http://getcoreinterface.typepad.com/blog/kevin-vandecar.html" rel="homepage" target="_blank" title="KDV">Kevin Vandecar</a></p>

BODY:
<h3>Who is this Kevin Vandecar guy?</h3>
<p>Since 2010 I have been working as a Developer Consulting Engineer with the <a class="zem_slink" title="Autodesk " rel="homepage" href="http://www.autodesk.com/adn" target="_blank">Autodesk Developer Network</a> team (DevTech). The DevTech team is tasked with providing pro-active support through the <a class="zem_slink" title="ADNOpen" rel="homepage" href="http://www.autodesk.com/adnopen" target="_blank">ADN Open program</a>, and also providing direct support for full ADN members. I am focused on support for the <a class="zem_slink" title="Autodesk 3ds Max" rel="homepage" href="http://www.autodesk.com/3dsmax" target="_blank">3ds Max</a> programming environments. I have a good deal of experience with <a class="zem_slink" title="3dsmaxdevcenter" rel="homepage" href="http://www.autodesk.com/develop3dsmax" target="_blank">3ds Max programming</a> and the purpose of this blog is to provide proactive details around 3ds Max customization. I will never say that I am an "expert" because 3ds Max has such a vast and rich history that no single person is likely to know everything! But through this blog I hope to help educate the community of 3ds Max programmers, developers, tinkerers, and the like. I also hope your expertise will help me! Please feel free to comment on the posts to help expand my knowledge and the community‚Äôs knowledge!</p>
<p>I enjoy helping people, so feel free to make suggestions for future posts <a href="mailto:kevin.vandecar@autodesk.com">by email</a>. I have always been interested in drafting, design and computer graphics. I have a bachelor‚Äôs degree in Engineering Graphics from <a class="zem_slink" title="Western Michigan University" rel="geolocation" href="http://maps.google.com/maps?ll=42.283178,-85.615219&amp;spn=0.01,0.01&amp;q=42.283178,-85.615219 (Western%20Michigan%20University)&amp;t=h" target="_blank">Western Michigan University</a> with a computer science minor. When I first started tinkering with computers, my first inclination was to customize my experience and is what lead me through the Computer Science formalities. I often learn things through experience and that stems from tinkering to solve problems. This quality also exhibits itself through me with my enjoyment of <a class="zem_slink" title="FoxMustang" rel="homepage" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_Mustang_(third_generation)#1987.E2.80.931993" target="_blank">auto</a>/<a class="zem_slink" title="ZRX" rel="homepage" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kawasaki_ZRX1200R" target="_blank">motorcycle</a> mechanics, building construction, <a class="zem_slink" title="rocketry" rel="homepage" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model_rocketry" target="_blank">model rocketry</a>, photography, etc.</p>
<p>Here is more detailed background information if you are interested‚Ä¶ I started my first period at Autodesk in 1990 working in product support as one of the first Developer Support technicians in <a class="zem_slink" title="Sausalito, California" rel="geolocation" href="http://maps.google.com/maps?ll=37.8591666667,-122.485277778&amp;spn=0.1,0.1&amp;q=37.8591666667,-122.485277778 (Sausalito%2C%20California)&amp;t=h" target="_blank">Sausalito, California</a> before the official ADN program even existed. Back in those days it was <a class="zem_slink" title="AutoCAD" rel="homepage" href="http://usa.autodesk.com/autocad/" target="_blank">AutoCAD</a> device driver support, along with LISP, ADS, and <a class="zem_slink" title="ObjectARX" rel="wikipedia" href="http://www.autodesk.com/objectarx" target="_blank">ObjectARX</a>. 3d Studio was also introduced as an Autodesk product in that timeframe and I was able to get my hands dirty with the IPAS plugin development environment.</p>
<p>I went on to work mostly with AutoCAD and AutoCAD OEM in various capacities; but always developer related technologies. This included developer support, API testing, documentation, and development. After working on AutoCAD OEM for a few years, I left Autodesk and worked for a large reseller/consulting firm that lead to development experience with AutoCAD Architecture and its Object Modeling Framework (OMF SDK).</p>
<p>After several years working on consulting projects, I returned to Autodesk in <a class="zem_slink" title="Manchester, New Hampshire" rel="geolocation" href="https://maps.google.com/maps?q=machester,+new+hampshire&amp;hl=en&amp;sll=44.001231,-71.566139&amp;sspn=6.954174,16.907959&amp;hnear=Manchester,+Hillsborough,+New+Hampshire&amp;t=m&amp;z=12&amp;iwloc=A" target="_blank">Manchester, New Hampshire</a>. I worked with the AutoCAD Architecture (ACA) engineering team for about 5 years. Most of the time was developing the .NET API for ACA, as well as assembling the OMF SDK. For my last year in AEC engineering, I spent some time working on the Revit API engineering team. It was then I realized I had strayed from my fundamental desire to tinker with APIs and decided to reset my career with 3ds Max! :-)</p>
<p>I can be contacted <a href="mailto:kevin.vandecar@autodesk.com">by email</a>, but please don't expect me to provide support. If you need support for our products or APIs, please visit Autodesk's <a href="http://support.autodesk.com/">support website</a>, use our <a href="http://discussion.autodesk.com/">discussion groups</a>, visit the <a href="http://area.autodesk.com/">AREA</a> community&nbsp; portal with dedicated M&amp;E blogs and discussion group or post a question via your reseller or the <a href="http://adn.autodesk.com/">Autodesk Developer Network website</a>, if you're a member.</p>
<p><strong>Disclaimer</strong><br />If you need an official Autodesk company response or a contact for press-related activities please contact <a href="http://www.autodesk.com/pressroom">Autodesk Public Relations</a>.</p>

In addition, my thoughts and opinions often change, and as a weblog is intended to provide a semi-permanent point-in-time snapshot you should not consider out-of-date posts to reflect my current thoughts and opinions.</p>
